Ta'zir for Calling Someone 'Kashhan' (Cuckold)
Determines ta'zir for calling someone a cuckold

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ta'zir for the term 'كشحان' and explain why it depends on its meaning as 'ديوث'.

Core Idea
Calling someone a cuckold (dayyuth) is a severe insult that obligates ta'zir in Hanafi fiqh.

This passage examines the Hanafi ruling on the term 'كشحان' (kashhan). While some lexicons associate it with the meaning 'cuckold' (ديوث), others link it to avoidance or distance. The relied-upon position in Fath al-Qadir holds that when used as an insult implying cuckoldry, ta'zir is wajib. Understanding this requires distinguishing between the term's possible roots and their legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Term in Dispute
The passage discusses 'كشحان' and its meaning. Note that it has two possible roots: one giving the meaning 'cuckold' (ديوث), another giving 'one who avoids' or 'distant relative'.
The root meaning determines whether the term is an insult.
2
Establish the Hanafi Position
The text states that when 'كشحان' means 'ديوث', ta'zir is wajib. This is the ruling in al-Mughrib and adopted as the truth in Fath al-Qadir.
The mufta bihi position is that ta'zir is applied.
3
Analyze the Dispute
Some Hanafis, based on alternative lexicons, may argue 'كشحان' is not an insult. The author of al-Mukhtasar apparently distinguished between the two meanings, causing some confusion.
The dispute does not affect the mufta bihi because the common usage equates to 'ديوث'.
4
Apply the Ruling
If someone says 'يا كشحان' to another, the ruling depends on intended meaning. If meant as cuckold, ta'zir is wajib. If meant as 'distant relative', no punishment.
The qadi must determine the context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكشحان فرأيت في بعض الحواشي أنه بالحاء المهملة. وفي المغرب : الكشحان الديوث الذي لا غيرة له، وكشحه وكشحته شتمته ويقال يا كشحان .اهـ. فحينئذ هو بمعنى القرطبان والديوث فيجب فيه التعزير ولذا قال في فتح القدير : والحق ما قاله بعض أصحابنا أنه يعزر في الكشحان إذ قيل إنه قريب من معنى القرطبان والديوث .اهـ. فما في المختصر مشكل لكن قال في ضياء الحلوم : كشح القوم عن الشيء إذا تفرقوا عنه وذهبوا وكشح له بالعداوة أضمرها في كشحه لأن العداوة فيه، وقيل الكاشح المتباعد عن مودة صاحبه من قولهم كشح القوم على الشيء إذا ذهبوا عنه، وفي الحديث أفضل الصدقة على ذي الرحم الكاشح فإن صح مجيء الكشحان منه فلا إشكال أنه ليس بمعنى القرطبان فلذا فرق المصنف بينهما.
As for 'الكشحان', I saw in some footnotes that it is with 'ha' (unpointed). In al-Mughrib: al-kashhan is the cuckold (dayyuth) who has no jealousy, and you say 'ya kashhan'. So then it means 'qurtaban' and 'dayyuth', and ta'zir is obligatory in it. Hence it is said in Fath al-Qadir: The truth is what some of our companions said, that he is ta'zir for 'kashhan' since it is said it is close in meaning to 'qurtaban' and 'dayyuth'. So what is in al-Mukhtasar is problematic. But it is said in Diya' al-Hulum: 'kashaha al-qawm 'an al-shay' if they dispersed from it and went away, and 'kashaha lahu bil-'adawah' he harbored enmity in his flank (kashh), and it is said 'al-kashih' is the one who distances himself from the friendship of his companion, from their saying 'kashaha al-qawm 'ala al-shay' if they went away from it. In the hadith: 'The best charity is to the kashih relative.' If the coming of 'kashhan' from this is correct, then there is no doubt that it is not in the meaning of 'qurtaban', so the author distinguished between them.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the term 'كشحان' (kashhan). The commentator discusses two possible meanings: one from al-Mughrib that it means 'ديوث' (cuckold), which is a serious insult requiring ta'zir; another from Diya' al-Hulum that it may mean a distant relative or one who avoids, which is not an insult. The commentator notes that the author (المصنف) of the matn (likely al-Nasafi) distinguished between the two roots, suggesting that 'كشحان' as a term for cuckold requires ta'zir. The Hanafi ruling: ta'zir is wajib for 'كشحان' when used to mean cuckold, which is the relied-upon position in Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
كشحان (kashhan): A term meaning cuckold (ديوث) according to al-Mughrib; also possibly meaning one who avoids, from root كشح.
ديوث (dayyuth): A cuckold; a man who has no jealousy regarding his wife's honor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling on saying 'يا كشحان' (O cuckold)?
A) No punishment because it is a neutral term.
B) Ta'zir is obligatory because it means cuckold, which is a severe insult.
C) Hadd al-qadhf is applied because it implies fornication.
D) Only a verbal admonition is given.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires ta'zir for the term 'كشحان' when used to mean cuckold, based on its common usage as a severe insult.

Ruling on Ta'zir for Terms 'Ablah' and 'Muwasswas'
Explains that 'ablah' is a praise and 'muwaswas' is insane, so no ta'zir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ta'zir for calling someone 'ablah' or 'muwaswas' and distinguish these from insulting terms like 'balid'.

Core Idea
Ablah' is praise, not insult; 'muwaswas' describes a condition; neither incurs ta'zir.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains two terms that might appear insulting but, according to Hanafi fiqh, do not warrant ta'zir (discretionary punishment). The key is the meaning and intent: 'ablah' is rooted in a hadith praising simplicity, and 'muwaswas' describes a person with obsessive whispers – a condition, not a slur. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of insult (sabb) and ta'zir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two terms
Recognize that the passage discusses 'ablah' (simpleton) and 'muwaswas' (obsessive whisperer).
2
Analyze 'ablah'
Trace the commentator's argument: he cites a hadith about most people of Paradise being simple and explains that 'ablah' means heedless of evil due to modesty, thus praiseworthy.
Contrast with 'balid' (dullard), which is an insult.
3
Analyze 'muwaswas'
Note the linguistic description: it indicates mental disturbance, not insult. The source quotes Abu al-Layth that divorce of such a person is invalid.
Hence calling someone 'muwaswas' is a description, not a slur.
4
Compare with 'balid'
The passage explicitly states that calling someone 'balid' incurs ta'zir because it attaches disgrace.
5
Conclude the ruling
Since neither 'ablah' nor 'muwaswas' is an insult, no ta'zir is applied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الأبله ففي ضياء الحلوم : البله الغفله وفي الحديث أكثر من يدخل الجنة «البله قيل: البله في أمر الدنيا بله. قال الزبرقان : خير أولادنا الأبله العقول أي الذي الغافلون عن الشر وإن لم يكن بهم لشدة حيائه كالأبله وهو عاقل .اهـ. فعلم أنها صفة مدح وإن كانت مفضولة بالنسبة لمن عنده حذق وعلم كما صرح به القرطبي في شرح مسلم في قوله عليه السلام «إن أهل الجنة يتراؤون الغرف فوقهم كالكوكب الدري وصرح البله وأن العلماء بأن المراد هم أهل الغرف فوقهم. وقيد بالأبله احترازاً عن البليد فإنه يعزر به. قال في الولوالجية: لو قال يا بليد يا قذر يجب فيه التعزير لأنه قذفه بمعصية ولأنه الحق الشين به اهـ. وفي كونه معصية نظر والظاهر التعليل الثاني. وأما الموسوس فضبطه في الظهيرية في فصل التعزير بكسر الواو، وفي المغرب : رجل موسوس بالكسر ولا يقال بالفتح ولكن موسوس له أو إليه أي ملقى إليه الوسوسة . وقال الليث : الوسوسة حديث النفس وإنما قيل موسوس عقله بما في ضميره وعن أبي الليث : لا يجوز طلاق الموسوس يعني المغلوب في عقله إذا تكلم تكلم بغير نظام اهـ .
As for 'الأبله' (simpleton): in Diya' al-Hulum, al-balah is heedlessness, and in the hadith: 'Most of the people of Paradise are the simple (al-bulh)'. It was said: al-balah is heedlessness in worldly matters. al-Zibriqan said: The best of our children is the simple of intellect (al-ablah al-'uqul), meaning those who are heedless of evil, even if they are not like that, due to intense modesty, like the simpleton while he is intelligent. So it is known that it is a praiseworthy attribute, even if it is less excellent than one who has skill and knowledge, as al-Qurtubi stated in his commentary on Muslim regarding the Prophet's saying: 'The people of Paradise will see the chambers above them like the brilliant planet' and he stated that the simple (al-bulh) are meant: that the scholars intend by them the people of the chambers above them. The restriction by 'ablah' is a precaution against 'balid' (dull), for he is ta'zir with it. It is said in al-Walwaljiyya: if one says 'O dullard, O filthy', ta'zir is obligatory because he has defamed him with a sin and because he attached disgrace to him. But in it being a sin there is consideration; the apparent reason is the second. And as for 'الموسوس' (obsessive whisperer): its pronunciation in al-Zahiriyya in the chapter of ta'zir is with kasra of the waw. In al-Mughrib: 'rajul muwaswis' with kasra, and it is not said with fatha, but 'muwaswas lahu' or 'ilayhi' meaning one to whom whisperings are cast. Al-Layth said: al-waswasa is self-talk, and it is only said 'muwaswis' in his mind what is in his conscience. From Abu al-Layth: the divorce of the muwaswis is not valid, meaning one overcome in his mind; when he speaks, he speaks without system.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on two terms: 'أبله' (simpleton) and 'موسوس' (obsessed with whisperings). For 'أبله', the commentator explains that it is actually a praiseworthy attribute, as mentioned in hadith, meaning one who is heedless of evil due to modesty. Therefore, no ta'zir. In contrast, 'بليد' (dullard) is an insult and requires ta'zir. For 'موسوس', it describes a person with mental disturbance; calling him by that is not an insult because it is a description of his condition. Hence, no ta'zir. The Hanafi ruling: no ta'zir for 'أبله' and 'موسوس'.

Key Terms
أبله (ablah): A simpleton; one heedless of evil due to modesty; a praiseworthy term.
موسوس (muwaswis): One who experiences obsessive whisperings (waswasa); a person with mental disturbance.
بليد (balid): Dullard; stupid person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is there no ta'zir for calling someone 'موسوس' (obsessive whisperer)?
A) Because it is a compliment.
B) Because it describes a mental condition and is not an insult.
C) Because the person is not responsible for his actions.
D) Because it is not a word used in custom.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, ta'zir for insults depends on the term's meaning; 'ablah' is praise, 'muwaswas' describes a condition, so no punishment.

Maximum and Minimum of Ta'zir with Abu Yusuf's Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ta'zir limits with prophetic hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maximum and minimum for ta'zir lashes and explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, including the underlying principle.

Core Idea
Ta'zir maximum is 39 lashes (Abu Hanifa) or 75 (Abu Yusuf); minimum is 3; must stay below hadd.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq sets the boundaries of ta'zir (discretionary punishment) within the Hanafi school. It establishes a clear maximum and minimum number of lashes, and notes a disagreement with the esteemed Abu Yusuf. The core principle is that ta'zir must never reach the level of a fixed hadd punishment, based on a prophetic warning. Understanding these limits is crucial for a judge administering discretionary punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the numerical limits
Locate the stated maximum (39 lashes) and minimum (3 lashes) of ta'zir. This is the relied-upon position.
The text explicitly says 'أكثر التعزير تسعة وثلاثون سوطاً وأقله ثلاثة'.
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that Abu Yusuf holds a different maximum: 75 lashes. This is a valid difference within the school.
The phrase 'وعن أبي يوسف أكثره خمسة وسبعون سوطاً' signals the dispute.
3
Examine the dalil
The hadith 'من بلغ حداً في غير حد فهو من المعتدين' is cited as the basis. Understand its meaning: applying a fixed hadd in a non-hadd context is transgression.
This hadith prohibits ta'zir from equalling or exceeding the lowest hadd.
4
Apply the principle
The lowest hadd in the Hanafi school is 40 lashes for drinking. Thus ta'zir must be less than 40, hence the maximum of 39. Abu Yusuf's 75 is close to the hadd of qadhf (80) but still below.
The principle is that ta'zir must be less than any hadd to avoid transgression.
5
Note the additional ruling
The passage also mentions that imprisonment after flogging is valid (sahih) and apparently obligatory (wajib). This supplements the ta'zir sentence.
The text says 'وصح حبسه بعد الضرب هكذا ذكر في بعض المواضع والظاهر أنه يجب'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأكثر التعزير تسعة وثلاثون سوطاً وأقله ثلاثة وصح حبسه بعد الضرب هكذا ذكر في بعض المواضع والظاهر أنه يجب اهـ . وعن أبي يوسف أكثره خمسة وسبعون سوطاً والأصل فيه الحديث من بلغ حداً في غير حد فهو من المعتدين» فتعذر تبليغه حداً بمعنى الآدمي فمعنى القذف به سلب الآدمية عن المقذوف .اهـ.
The maximum of ta'zir is thirty-nine lashes, and its minimum is three, and his imprisonment after beating is valid. Thus it is mentioned in some places, and the apparent is that it is obligatory. From Abu Yusuf: its maximum is seventy-five lashes. The basis for it (i.e., the principle) is the hadith: 'Whoever reaches (applies) a hadd in other than a hadd is among the transgressors.' So it is impossible to make it reach a hadd in the sense of a human being, so the meaning of qadhf by it is the removal of humanity from the accused.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the maximum number of lashes in ta'zir. The relied-upon position (Abu Hanifa) is that the maximum is 39, which is less than the minimum hadd (which is 40 for drinking). The minimum is 3 lashes. Abu Yusuf holds that the maximum is 75, based on a hadith that prohibits reaching a fixed hadd in non-hadd punishments. The commentator explains that the basis for limiting ta'zir below hadd is to avoid transgressing. There is also a note about the meaning of qadhf: it strips the accused of humanity.

Key Terms
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment, with maximum 39 lashes (Abu Hanifa) and minimum 3.
حد (hadd): Fixed punishment for certain crimes; ta'zir must not reach the level of hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the maximum number of lashes for ta'zir?
A) 75 lashes
B) 39 lashes
C) 40 lashes
D) 99 lashes

Key Takeaway
The maximum ta'zir is 39 lashes according to the relied-upon Hanafi position, with a minority view of 75 by Abu Yusuf; the minimum is 3, and the principle is to stay below all hudud.

Ta'zir for the Musawwas (One Afflicted with Waswas)
Defines the term musawwas and rules that ta'zir applies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the musawwas and state the Hanafi ruling that ta'zir applies instead of hadd.

Core Idea
A person afflicted with waswas to the point of incoherent speech receives ta'zir, not hadd.

The musawwas is one whose mind is so overcome by whispers that his speech becomes disordered. This lesson examines the definition of such a person and the legal consequences: while his mental state invalidates some of his actions (like divorce), he is not completely exempt from punishment; the Hanafi school prescribes ta'zir (discretionary punishment) instead of the fixed hadd penalty. We will explore the lexicographical and legal definitions provided in the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling statement
Begin by noting the clear ruling: 'موسوس يعزر' — the musawwas is given ta'zir. This is the core hukm from the matn.
2
Analyze the linguistic definition
Examine the philological sources: the correct pronunciation (kasra on waw), the definitions from al-Layth (waswasa as self-talk), and the clarification that 'musawwas' describes one whose conscience is disturbed.
Understanding the linguistic root helps grasp the legal concept of diminished capacity.
3
Examine the legal implication: divorce invalid
Note the quote from Abu al-Layth: the divorce of a musawwas is invalid because his speech is without order. This illustrates that his mental state affects the validity of his utterances.
This shows that the musawwas is not fully legally responsible.
4
Understand the distinction between ta'zir and hadd
The musawwas is given ta'zir rather than hadd for offenses like slander. Ta'zir is discretionary and can be adjusted to the offender's condition, while hadd requires full legal capacity.
Ta'zir is less severe and can be applied flexibly.
5
Recognize the principle of diminished capacity
The passage establishes that when mental capacity is impaired (but not completely absent), the punishment is reduced from fixed hadd to discretionary ta'zir. This reflects the Hanafi concern for proportionality and intent.
This principle applies to other areas of fiqh as well.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موسوس يعزر. وأما الموسوس فضبطه في الظهيرية في فصل التعزير بكسر الواو، وفي المغرب : رجل موسوس بالكسر ولا يقال بالفتح ولكن موسوس له أو إليه أي ملقى إليه الوسوسة . وقال الليث : الوسوسة حديث النفس وإنما قيل موسوس عقله بما في ضميره وعن أبي الليث : لا يجوز طلاق الموسوس يعني المغلوب في عقله إذا تكلم تكلم بغير نظام اهـ . لأنه يحدث وعن الحاكم: هو المضاب
The musawwas is given ta'zir. As for the musawwas, in al-Zahira it is recorded in the section on ta'zir with a kasra on the waw. And in al-Mughrib: a man who is musawwas (with kasra) and it is not said with fatah, but rather musawwas lahu or ilayhi, meaning one whom waswas is cast. Al-Layth said: Waswasa is self-talk, and it is only said 'musawwas' (his mind) because of what is in his conscience. And from Abu al-Layth: The divorce of a musawwas is not valid, meaning one who is overcome in his intellect, when he speaks he speaks without order. Because he speaks [randomly]. And from al-Hakim: He is the one who is confused.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling statement. The matn from Kanz al-Daqaiq states simply 'موسوس يعزر' — the musawwas is given ta'zir. The sharh then explains who the musawwas is: linguistically, it is a person affected by waswas (whispers), often from the devil, to the point that his speech becomes disordered. The author cites lexicographical sources: al-Zahira records the pronunciation with kasra, and al-Mughrib defines it as one to whom waswas is cast. Al-Layth defines waswasa as internal speech. Importantly, Abu al-Layth states that the divorce of a musawwas (who is mentally overcome) is invalid because his speech is not coherent. From this, the ruling is that ta'zir is applied to the musawwas when he commits an offense like qadhf (slander) because his condition does not make him fully liable for hadd, but ta'zir is still appropriate. The passage ends with a quote from al-Hakim that he is 'المضاب' (the confused one), confirming his diminished capacity.

Key Terms
الموسوس (al-musawwas): The one who is overwhelmed by waswas (whispers) to the point that his speech is disordered and he is considered mentally deficient.
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for offenses that do not have a prescribed hadd or kaffarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for the musawwas?
A) He is given the hadd punishment for qadhf.
B) He is given ta'zir.
C) He is completely exempt from punishment.
D) He is imprisoned indefinitely.

Key Takeaway
The musawwas, whose speech is disordered due to waswas, receives ta'zir instead of hadd, and his divorce is invalid.

Ta'zir for Calling Someone 'Kashhan'
Definition and ruling of 'kashhan' with lexical exploration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of ta'zir for uttering 'kashhan' and explain the basis for the Hanafi position.

Core Idea
Calling someone 'kashhan' is an insult akin to 'dayyuth' and thus requires ta'zir.

This lesson examines a disputed term: 'kashhan'. Some lexicographers equate it with 'dayyuth' (cuckold), a clear insult, while others derive it from a root meaning enmity or distance. The Hanafi school, as expressed in Fath al-Qadir, takes the former view and holds that ta'zir is obligatory. We will explore the linguistic evidence and the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its potential ruling
The act is uttering 'ya kashhan' to another person. Determine whether this falls under insult (sabb) requiring ta'zir.
Ta'zir is a discretionary punishment for offenses without fixed hadd.
2
Examine the primary definition from al-Mughrib
According to al-Mughrib, 'kashhan' means 'dayyuth' (cuckold), one lacking gheerah. This is a direct insult to honor.
This definition supports the imposition of ta'zir.
3
Consider the alternative derivation from Diya' al-Hulum
An alternative root suggests 'kashhan' refers to one who is distant or harbors enmity, which may not be an insult. The author notes this to show why some texts distinguish it from 'dayyuth'.
If this meaning is correct, ta'zir may not apply.
4
Apply the Hanafi tarjih
Fath al-Qadir endorses the view that ta'zir is required, because the common understanding is that 'kashhan' is an insult similar to 'dayyuth'. This is the mufta bihi position.
The weight of later Hanafi authority supports this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكشحان فرأيت في بعض الحواشي أنه بالحاء المهملة. وفي المغرب : الكشحان الديوث الذي لا غيرة له، وكشحه وكشحته شتمته ويقال يا كشحان .اهـ. فحينئذ هو بمعنى القرطبان والديوث فيجب فيه التعزير ولذا قال في فتح القدير : والحق ما قاله بعض أصحابنا أنه يعزر في الكشحان إذ قيل إنه قريب من معنى القرطبان والديوث .اهـ. فما في المختصر مشكل لكن قال في ضياء الحلوم : كشح القوم عن الشيء إذا تفرقوا عنه وذهبوا وكشح له بالعداوة أضمرها في كشحه لأن العداوة فيه، وقيل الكاشح المتباعد عن مودة صاحبه من قولهم كشح القوم على الشيء إذا ذهبوا عنه، وفي الحديث أفضل الصدقة على ذي الرحم الكاشح فإن صح مجيء الكشحان منه فلا إشكال أنه ليس بمعنى القرطبان فلذا فرق المصنف بينهما.
As for al-kashhan, I saw in some glosses that it is with the unpointed ha (ح). And in al-Mughrib: al-kashhan is the dayyuth, the one without protective jealousy. And kashahahu and kashahatahu means he insulted him, and it is said 'ya kashhan'. So it is synonymous with qurtaban and dayyuth, so ta'zir is obligatory for it. That is why it is said in Fath al-Qadir: The correct is what some of our companions said, that ta'zir is given for saying 'kashhan' because it is close in meaning to qurtaban and dayyuth. So what is in al-Mukhtasar is problematic. But it is said in Diya' al-Hulum: kashaha al-qawm 'an al-shay' means they dispersed and went away from it, and kashaha lahu bi-l-'adawah means he harbored enmity in his flank (kashh) because enmity is there. And it is said al-kashih is the one who distances himself from his friend's affection. And in the hadith: 'The best charity is to a relative who is kashih.' If it is established that kashhan comes from this, then there is no doubt that it is not synonymous with qurtaban, so the author distinguished between them.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling statement concerning the word 'kashhan'. The author begins by noting a variant spelling with ح (ha) instead of خ (kha). He then cites al-Mughrib defining kashhan as dayyuth (cuckold) — a person lacking gheerah (protective jealousy). Because this is an insult imputing a moral failing, it is similar to qadhf (slander) and thus requires ta'zir. The author quotes Fath al-Qadir supporting this view. However, he then presents an alternative interpretation from Diya' al-Hulum, which derives kashhan from a root meaning distance and enmity, and cites a hadith about charity to a 'kashih' relative, which suggests a different meaning. If this is correct, then kashhan is not synonymous with dayyuth, and the author of al-Mukhtasar distinguished between them. In either case, the relied-upon position appears to be that calling someone kashhan does require ta'zir, as it is an insult akin to qadhf.

Key Terms
الكشحان (al-kashhan): A term of insult meaning dayyuth (cuckold) or one who lacks gheerah; also possibly derived from distance/enmity.
الديوث (al-dayyuth): A cuckold; one who lacks protective jealousy over his family.
التعزير (al-ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for offenses that do not have a fixed hadd penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Hadd of qadhf is required.
D) It is makruh but not punishable.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that ta'zir is required for calling someone 'kashhan', despite a lexical alternative.

Ta'zir for Calling Someone 'Ablah' vs 'Balid'
Defines two terms and their ta'zir consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the legal treatment of calling someone 'ablah' versus 'balid' and state the Hanafi ruling on ta'zir.

Core Idea
Calling someone 'ablah' is praiseworthy and exempt from ta'zir; 'balid' is an insult requiring ta'zir.

This lesson examines a subtle distinction in Hanafi ta'zir law: the difference between describing someone as 'ablah' (simpleton) and 'balid' (stupid). While both words relate to intelligence, the Hanafi school treats them very differently due to their connotations in the Shari'ah. Understanding this distinction reveals how the law takes into account linguistic and social context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two terms
Read the passage and note the definitions of 'ablah' and 'balid'. What does each term imply about the person?
Ablah is described as heedless of evil due to shyness; balid is a dull, stupid person.
2
Analyze the evidence for 'ablah'
What hadith and scholarly commentary establish 'ablah' as praiseworthy? Why does the author conclude it is not subject to ta'zir?
The hadith says most of Paradise's inhabitants are the 'ablah', and al-Qurtubi confirms they are the people of the highest chambers.
3
Analyze the evidence for 'balid'
According to al-Walwalijiyya, why is calling someone 'balid' subject to ta'zir? Identify the two reasons given.
It is considered qadhf bi-ma'siyah (imputation of sin) and attaches disgrace to the person.
4
Apply the distinction
Given the ruling, how would a Hanafi judge rule if someone is called 'ablah' vs 'balid'? What is the practical consequence?
No ta'zir for 'ablah'; ta'zir for 'balid'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الأبله ففي ضياء الحلوم : البله الغفله وفي الحديث أكثر من يدخل الجنة «البله قيل: البله في أمر الدنيا بله. قال الزبرقان : خير أولادنا الأبله العقول أي الذي الغافلون عن الشر وإن لم يكن بهم لشدة حيائه كالأبله وهو عاقل .اهـ. فعلم أنها صفة مدح وإن كانت مفضولة بالنسبة لمن عنده حذق وعلم كما صرح به القرطبي في شرح مسلم في قوله عليه السلام «إن أهل الجنة يتراؤون الغرف فوقهم كالكوكب الدري وصرح . البله وأن العلماء بأن المراد هم أهل الغرف فوقهم. وقيد بالأبله احترازاً عن البليد فإنه يعزر به. قال في الولوالجية: لو قال يا بليد يا قذر يجب فيه التعزير لأنه قذفه بمعصية ولأنه الحق الشين به اهـ. وفي كونه معصية نظر والظاهر التعليل الثاني.
As for al-ablah, in Diya' al-Hulum: al-balah is heedlessness. And in the hadith: 'Most of those who enter Paradise are the ablah (simpletons).' It is said: al-balah is in worldly matters. Al-Zibriqan said: The best of our children is the ablah-ul-'uqul (the foolish-minded), i.e., those who are heedless of evil even if not due to anything, due to intense shyness like the ablah, and he is intelligent. So it is known that it is a praiseworthy attribute, even if it is inferior compared to one who has skill and knowledge, as al-Qurtubi explained in his commentary on Muslim in the Prophet's saying: 'The people of Paradise will see the chambers above them like shining stars.' And he stated that the ablah are meant as the people of the chambers above them. And he specified 'ablah' to avoid the balid, because the balid is given ta'zir for it. He said in al-Walwalijiyya: If he says 'O balid, O dirty,' ta'zir is obligatory because he has slandered him with a sin and because he has attached disgrace to him. There is consideration in it being a sin, and the apparent reason is the second one.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'ablah' and distinguishes it from 'balid' for the purpose of ta'zir. The author first explains that 'ablah' (simpleton) is a praiseworthy attribute in Islamic tradition, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) said most of the inhabitants of Paradise are the 'ablah' — meaning those who are heedless of evil due to innocence and shyness, not due to stupidity. Al-Qurtubi's commentary confirms this, indicating that the ablah are the people of the highest chambers in Paradise. Therefore, calling someone 'ablah' is not an insult and does not warrant ta'zir. In contrast, 'balid' (stupid, dull) is a blameworthy attribute. The author cites al-Walwalijiyya stating that if one says 'ya balid, ya qadhir' (O stupid, O dirty), ta'zir is obligatory because it is an imputation of sin (qadhf bi-ma'siyah) and because it attaches disgrace to the person. The author notes that there is doubt about it being a sin, but the second reason (attaching disgrace) is apparent. Thus, the ruling: 'ablah' is not subject to ta'zir, while 'balid' is.

Key Terms
الأبله (al-ablah): A person of guileless simplicity, often praiseworthy in Islam for being heedless of evil out of shyness.
البليد (al-balid): A stupid, dull person; an insult that attaches disgrace.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) يا بليد
B) يا قذر
C) يا أبله
D) يا ديوك

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between 'ablah' (praiseworthy naivety) and 'balid' (blameworthy stupidity) for the purpose of ta'zir.

Maximum Ta'zir Lashes: Dispute Between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
Discusses the maximum number of lashes in ta'zir with intra-Hanafi disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar on the maximum ta'zir lashes and identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.

Core Idea
Ta'zir has a ceiling: Abu Yusuf's 75 lashes for free persons is the operative view.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute on the maximum corporal punishment in ta'zir. While the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq states 39 lashes, later authorities favour Abu Yusuf's opinion of 75 for free persons, based on a Companion report. The dispute hinges on whether to analogize ta'zir to the hadd of slaves (40) or free persons (80).

Guided Path
1
Identify the base position from the matn
Kanz al-Daqaiq states 'the maximum of ta'zir is thirty-nine lashes' – this is Abu Hanifa's view.
2
Contrast with Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf holds the maximum is 75 for a free person and 39 for a slave. This is supported by a report from Ali ibn Abi Talib.
The text says 'وعن أبي يوسف أكثره خمسة وسبعون سوطاً'.
3
Examine the dalil for both views
Both use the hadith 'من بلغ حداً في غير حد فهو من المعتدين' (whoever reaches a hadd in a non-hadd matter is a transgressor). Abu Hanifa analogizes to the lesser hadd (slave: 40) and stays below (39). Abu Yusuf analogizes to the greater hadd (free: 80) and subtracts 5.
Abu Hanifa's qiyas: ta'zir < minimum hadd (40). Abu Yusuf's: ta'zir < maximum hadd (80) → 75.
4
Note Zufar's view
Zufar reduces only one lash from 80, giving 79 (or for slaves? The text is ambiguous but likely 79 for free). This is said to be the pure qiyas.
Text: 'ينقص منها سوطاً وهو قول زفر وهو القياس'.
5
Determine the tarjih (preferred view)
The author declares Abu Yusuf's view as 'asahh' (most correct) and quotes al-Hawi al-Qudsi: 'وبه نأخذ' (we take it). Thus the mufta bihi is 75 for free, 39 for slave.
The text: 'فعلم أن الأصح قول أبي يوسف'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وأكثر التعزير تسعة وثلاثون سوطاً وعن أبي يوسف أكثره خمسة وسبعون سوطاً والأصل فيه الحديث من بلغ حداً في غير حد فهو من المعتدين» فتعذر تبليغه حداً بمعنى الآدمي فمعنى القذف به سلب الآدمية عن المقذوف .اهـ. وروي أنه بالإجماع غير أن أبا حنيفة اعتبر أدنى الحدود وهو حد العبيد لأن مطلق ما روينا يتناوله وأقله أربعون، وأبو يوسف اعتبر حد الأحرار لأنهم هم الأصول وأقله ثمانون فلا بد من النقص ففي رواية عنه ينقص خمسة وروي ذلك عن علي رضي الله عنه وهو ظاهر الرواية عن أبي يوسف كما في فتح القدير قيل : وليس فيه معنى معقول فلا يضره لأنه قلد فيه علياً رضي الله عنه، ويجب تقليد الصحابي فيما لا يدرك بالرأي. وفي رواية ينقص سوط. وفي الحاوي القدسي قال أبو يوسف أكثره في العبد تسعة وثلاثون سوطاً، وفي الحر خمسة وسبعون سوطاً وبه نأخذ اهـ. فعلم أن الأصح قول أبي يوسف. وفي المجتبى : ينقص منها سوطاً وهو قول زفر وهو القياس وهو الأصح اهـ. وفي فتح القدير : وبما ذكرنا من تقدير أكثره بتسعة وثلاثين يعرف أن ما ذكر مما تقدم من أنه ليس في التعزير شيء مقدر بل مفوض إلى رأي الإمام أي من أنواعه فإنه يكون بالضرب وبغيره مما تقدم ذكره أما إن اقتضى رأيه الضرب في خصوص الواقعة فإنه حينئذ لا يزيد على تسعة وثلاثين اهـ. وقد وقع لي تردد في مسألة وهي أن انساناً لو ضرب إنساناً بغير حق أكثر من أكثر التعزير ورفع إلى القاضي وثبت عليه أنه ضربه مثلاً خمسين سوطاً كيف يعزره القاضي؟ فإنه إن ضربه خمسين زاد على أكثر التعزير، وإن اقتصر على الأكثر لم يكن مستوفياً لحق المضروب إلا أن يقال: إن حقه التعزير لا القصاص وقد صرح في الخانية أن مما يجب التعزير به الضرب
His saying: (The maximum of ta'zir is thirty-nine lashes) and from Abu Yusuf its maximum is seventy-five lashes. And the basis for that is the hadith: 'Whoever reaches a hadd in a non-hadd [matter] is among the transgressors.' It is difficult to apply a hadd meaning an Adamic [right?]. So the meaning of qadhf with it is stripping the person of his humanity. And it is reported that it is by consensus, except that Abu Hanifa considered the lower of the two hadd punishments, which is the hadd of slaves, because the absolute [meaning] of what we narrated includes it, and its minimum is forty. And Abu Yusuf considered the hadd of free persons because they are the originals, and its minimum is eighty, so a reduction is necessary. In one narration from him he reduces by five, and that is reported from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him), and it is the apparent narration from Abu Yusuf as in Fath al-Qadir. It is said: There is no rational meaning in it, so it does not harm him because he followed Ali in it, and it is obligatory to follow a Companion in matters that cannot be reached by opinion. And in another narration he reduces by one lash. And in al-Hawi al-Qudsi, Abu Yusuf said: Its maximum in a slave is thirty-nine lashes, and in a free person it is seventy-five lashes, and we take that. So it is known that the correct view is that of Abu Yusuf. And in al-Mujtaba: He reduces from it one lash, and that is the view of Zufar, and it is the qiyas, and it is the most correct. And in Fath al-Qadir: By what we have mentioned of estimating its maximum at thirty-nine, it is known that what was mentioned earlier that there is nothing fixed in ta'zir but is left to the opinion of the Imam — that applies to its types, for it may be with beating or other than that. But if his opinion necessitates beating in a particular incident, then he should not exceed thirty-nine. And I have had hesitation in a case: if a person strikes another unjustly more than the maximum of ta'zir, and it is brought to the judge and it is proven that he struck him, for example, fifty lashes: how should the judge administer ta'zir? If he strikes him fifty, he exceeds the maximum; if he restricts to the maximum, he does not fulfill the right of the victim. Unless it is said: His right is ta'zir, not qisas. And it is stated in al-Khaniyya that among the things that necessitate ta'zir is beating.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the maximum number of lashes in ta'zir. The matn from Kanz al-Daqaiq states the maximum is 39 lashes, following Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf opined that the maximum is 75 lashes for a free person and 39 for a slave. The basis is a hadith that prohibits exceeding the hadd in non-hadd matters. Abu Hanifa analogizes ta'zir to the hadd of slaves (40 lashes for qadhf), so the maximum is just below that (39). Abu Yusuf analogizes to the hadd of free persons (80), and reduces by 5 to 75, following a report from Ali ibn Abi Talib. Zufar held it should be reduced by 1 (79 for free? Actually from the text: 'ينقص سوط' meaning 79? Or from 80? The text is unclear. Later, al-Hawi al-Qudsi records that Abu Yusuf set 39 for slaves and 75 for free, and that is the relied-upon view. Some later authorities, like Fath al-Qadir, note that although the maximum is set, ta'zir in general is discretionary and can be with various means; if beating is chosen, the maximum is 39 or 75? The text ends with a hypothetical about exceeding ta'zir and what the judge should do. The relied-upon position is that the maximum for ta'zir by beating is 39 lashes according to the matn, but according to Abu Yusuf's view (which is considered 'asahh' in this passage) is 75 for free persons. The author seems to lean towards Abu Yusuf's view.

Key Terms
التعزير (al-ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for offenses without a fixed hadd; in this context, lashes are discussed.
الحد (al-hadd): Fixed corporal punishment prescribed by the Shari'ah for specific crimes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school sets a maximum for ta'zir to avoid resembling hadd; the operative view is 75 lashes for free persons and 39 for slaves.

The Minimum Amount of Ta'zir: Three Lashes vs Judicial Discretion
Dispute on whether the minimum is fixed at three lashes or left to the judge's discretion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimum ta'zir lashes and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The minimum ta'zir lashes is three according to al-Quduri but discretionary according to later mashayikh.

The Hanafi school discusses whether ta'zir requires a fixed minimum number of lashes. In this passage, the commentator presents two views: a fixed minimum of three lashes from al-Quduri, and a flexible approach based on judicial discretion from the mashayikh. Understanding this dispute reveals how later Hanafi scholars shifted towards purposive reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the matn's position
Identify the ruling in the matn: the minimum is three lashes. Recognize that this is attributed to al-Quduri and is considered zahir al-riwayah.
The reasoning is that fewer than three do not deter (zajr).
2
Identify the mashayikh's position
The later mashayikh hold that there is no fixed minimum; it is left to the judge's discretion based on what achieves deterrence.
They argue that deterrence varies by individual, so a fixed number may be unnecessary.
3
Analyse the reasoning
The commentator points out that the purpose (zajr) can be achieved with fewer lashes if the judge deems it sufficient.
This is a rational (dalil aqli) argument based on the purpose of ta'zir.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a judge knows that one lash will deter a particular offender, the matn requires at least three, while the mashayikh allow one.
This affects sentencing in real cases.
5
Compare authority levels
The matn represents zahir al-riwayah; the mashayikh represent later authorities (fatawa mutakhkhirin). The passage does not give a clear tarjih, but later practice often follows the mashayikh.
This is an example of how later Hanafi scholarship can override earlier texts when the reasoning supports the purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وأقله ثلاثة) أي أقل التعزير بالضرب ثلاثة أسواط وهكذا ذكر القدوري فكأنه يرى أن ما دونها لا يقع به الزجر وليس كذلك، بل يختلف ذلك باختلاف الأشخاص فلا معنى لتقديره مع حصول المقصود بدونه فيكون مفوضاً إلى رأي القاضي يقيمه بقدر ما يرى المصلحة فيه على ما بينا تفاصيله وعليه مشايخنا؛ كذا في التبيين والحاصل أن على ما في المختصر لو علم القاضي أن الزجر يحصل بسوط لا يكتفى به بل لا بد من الثلاثة وعلى قول المشايخ يكتفى به اهـ.
His saying: (And its minimum is three) meaning the minimum of ta'zir by beating is three lashes. And thus al-Quduri mentioned it, as if he holds that what is less than that does not deter. But it is not so; rather, it differs according to individuals. So there is no meaning in fixing it when the purpose is achieved without it. So it is delegated to the opinion of the judge: he imposes it according to what he sees of maslaha, as we have detailed. And upon this are our mashayikh. This is in al-Tabyin. The conclusion is that according to what is in al-Mukhtasar, if the judge knows that deterrence is achieved by one lash, he cannot be satisfied with it; rather, three are necessary. And according to the saying of the mashayikh, he can be satisfied with it.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the minimum number of lashes in ta'zir. The matn from Kanz al-Daqaiq states that the minimum is three lashes, following the view of al-Quduri. The reasoning is that fewer than three does not achieve deterrence (zajr). However, the commentator notes that this is not necessarily true; deterrence varies by individual. Therefore, the later mashayikh (senior scholars) hold that the minimum is not fixed but is left to the judge's discretion based on what achieves the purpose of ta'zir. The conclusion in al-Tabyin is that according to the matn (al-Mukhtasar), the judge must give at least three lashes even if he knows one would suffice, but according to the mashayikh, he may suffice with one. This reflects a shift from a fixed minimum to a discretionary approach, emphasizing the purpose of ta'zir (reform and deterrence) over a rigid number.

Key Terms
الزجر (al-zajr): Deterrence; the purpose of ta'zir is to deter the offender from repeating the offense.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mashayikh (later Hanafi scholars), what is the minimum number of lashes for ta'zir?
A) Three lashes
B) One lash
C) No fixed minimum; left to judge's discretion
D) Ten lashes

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the minimum ta'zir lashes is disputed: fixed at three by early authorities but left to judicial discretion by later scholars based on the purpose of deterrence.

Combining Imprisonment with Flogging in Ta'zir
Ruling that combining imprisonment with flogging is valid in ta'zir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining imprisonment with flogging in ta'zir and explain the reasoning behind it.

Core Idea
In ta'zir, the judge may combine imprisonment and flogging because ta'zir is flexible and the Shari'ah permits it.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a key point in Hanafi ta'zir law: a judge may imprison an offender after flogging him, combining both punishments. It distinguishes ta'zir from hadd, where such combination is not allowed before proof, and affirms the judge's discretion in choosing both penalties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is combining imprisonment with flogging in ta'zir. The ruling is permissibility (ja'iz).
2
Locate the reasoning
The passage states it is permissible because ta'zir is a discretionary punishment and the Shari'ah has allowed imprisonment alone, so adding it to flogging is also allowed.
3
Note the distinction from hadd
In hadd, pre-trial detention is not allowed; in ta'zir, imprisonment is part of the punishment and can be combined with flogging.
4
Understand the scope of imprisonment
Imprisonment is absolute, including house arrest or prison, giving the judge further discretion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وصح حبسه بعد الضرب أي جاز للحاكم أن يحبس العاصي بعد الضرب فيجمع بين حبسه وضربه لأنه صلح تعزيراً وقد ورد به الشرع في الجملة حتى جاز أن يكتفى به فجاز أن يضم إليه، ولهذا لم يشرع في التعزير بالتهمة قبل ثبوته كما شرع في الحد لأنه من التعزير . أطلق في الحبس فشمل الحبس في البيت والسجن . قال في الحاوي القدسي : وقد يكون التعزير بالحبس في بيته أو في السجن اهـ.
His saying: (And his imprisonment after flogging is valid) meaning it is permissible for the judge to imprison the sinner after flogging, thus combining imprisonment and flogging. Because it is part of ta'zir, and the Shari'ah has generally allowed it to the extent that it is permissible to suffice with it, so it is permissible to add it to [flogging]. For this reason, it is not legislated in ta'zir on suspicion before its proof as it is legislated in hadd, because it is part of ta'zir. He made imprisonment absolute, so it includes imprisonment in the house and in prison. He said in al-Hawi al-Qudsi: Ta'zir may be by imprisonment in his house or in prison.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: it is permissible for a judge to imprison a person who has committed a ta'zir offense after having flogged him, combining both punishments. The reasoning is that ta'zir is discretionary and the Shari'ah has allowed various forms, including imprisonment alone. Since imprisonment alone is allowed, adding it to flogging is also allowed. The author distinguishes ta'zir from hadd: in hadd, imprisonment before proof is not allowed (referring to pre-trial detention), but in ta'zir it is part of the punishment. The type of imprisonment is broad, including house arrest or jail. This gives the judge flexibility in tailoring the punishment to the offender.

Key Terms
الحبس (al-habs): Imprisonment; one form of ta'zir punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Yes, because ta'zir is flexible.
C) Only if the offense is very serious.
D) Only if the offender is a repeat criminal.

Key Takeaway
Combining imprisonment with flogging in ta'zir is permissible because ta'zir is discretionary and the judge may tailor punishments.

Maximum Ta'zir Lashes: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Discusses the maximum number of lashes in ta'zir, with differing opinions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three intra-Hanafi opinions on the maximum ta'zir lashes, explain the basis of each, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Ta'zir lashes are capped: 39 for a slave, 75 for a free person—Abu Yusuf's view is the operative ruling.

The Hanafi school permits ta'zir (discretionary punishment) but disagrees on the maximum number of lashes. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the ikhtilaf among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar, and settles on Abu Yusuf's opinion as the relied-upon position. Understanding this dispute highlights the role of qiyas and the authority of Companion reports in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
List the maximum number of lashes proposed by each imam for a slave and a free person. Abu Hanifa: 40 for slave (and presumably 40 for free, based on the lowest hadd). Abu Yusuf: 39 for slave, 75 for free. Zufar: 39 for slave, 79 for free.
The numbers are derived from analogies to fixed hadd punishments.
2
Analyze the basis of each
Abu Hanifa: qiyas to the slave's hadd (40) as the minimum of fixed punishments. Abu Yusuf: qiyas to the free hadd (80) decreased by 5 based on a report from Ali (RA). Zufar: qiyas to the free hadd decreased by 1 (pure analogy).
Abu Yusuf's decrease relies on a Companion report, which is binding in non-rational matters.
3
Understand the tarjih mechanism
The text declares Abu Yusuf's view as zahir al-riwayah and the correct opinion. Al-Hawi al-Qudsi and Fath al-Qadir prefer it. The reliance on a Companion report gives it additional weight.
Tarjih is based on transmission authority, not just rational strength.
4
Apply the mufta bihi
The operative ruling: maximum ta'zir lashes for a slave is 39, for a free person 75. This applies when the judge chooses flogging; other ta'zir methods (e.g., imprisonment) are also permissible.
The cap is specific to flogging; the judge may use other means without such numerical limits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وروي أنه بالإجماع غير أن أبا حنيفة اعتبر أدنى الحدود وهو حد العبيد لأن مطلق ما روينا يتناوله وأقله أربعون، وأبو يوسف اعتبر حد الأحرار لأنهم هم الأصول وأقله ثمانون فلا بد من النقص ففي رواية عنه ينقص خمسة وروي ذلك عن علي رضي الله عنه وهو ظاهر الرواية عن أبي يوسف كما في فتح القدير قيل : وليس فيه معنى معقول فلا يضره لأنه قلد فيه علياً رضي الله عنه، ويجب تقليد الصحابي فيما لا يدرك بالرأي. وفي رواية ينقص سوط. وفي الحاوي القدسي قال أبو يوسف أكثره في العبد تسعة وثلاثون سوطاً، وفي الحر خمسة وسبعون سوطاً وبه نأخذ اهـ. فعلم أن الأصح قول أبي يوسف. وفي المجتبى : ينقص منها سوطاً وهو قول زفر وهو القياس وهو الأصح اهـ. وفي فتح القدير : وبما ذكرنا من تقدير أكثره بتسعة وثلاثين يعرف أن ما ذكر مما تقدم من أنه ليس في التعزير شيء مقدر بل مفوض إلى رأي الإمام أي من أنواعه فإنه يكون بالضرب وبغيره مما تقدم ذكره أما إن اقتضى رأيه الضرب في خصوص الواقعة فإنه حينئذ لا يزيد على تسعة وثلاثين اهـ.
And it is narrated that it is by consensus, except that Abu Hanifa considered the lowest of the boundaries, which is the punishment of slaves, because the absolute (text) we narrated encompasses it, and its minimum is forty. Abu Yusuf considered the punishment of free persons because they are the originals, and its minimum is eighty, so there must be a decrease. In one narration from him (Abu Yusuf), it is decreased by five, and that is narrated from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him), and that is the apparent narration from Abu Yusuf as in Fath al-Qadir. It is said: There is no rational meaning in it, so it does not harm him because he followed Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) in it, and it is obligatory to follow a Companion in matters not perceived by opinion. In another narration, it is decreased by one lash. In al-Hawi al-Qudsi, Abu Yusuf said: Its maximum for a slave is thirty-nine lashes, and for a free person is seventy-five lashes, and we take that. So it is known that the correct opinion is that of Abu Yusuf. In al-Mujtaba: It is decreased by one lash, and that is the opinion of Zufar, and it is the analogy, and it is the most correct. In Fath al-Qadir: By what we have mentioned of estimating its maximum at thirty-nine, it is known that what was mentioned previously that there is no fixed measure in ta'zir, but rather it is delegated to the opinion of the Imam, meaning in its types, for it may be by flogging and other than that as previously mentioned. However, if his opinion requires flogging in a particular incident, then he should not exceed thirty-nine.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the maximum number of lashes in ta'zir (discretionary punishment) for a slave and a free person. The author begins by stating that there is consensus on the permissibility of ta'zir, but the amount is disputed. Abu Hanifa analogizes ta'zir to the minimum fixed punishment (hadd), which is the punishment of a slave (40 lashes for false accusation). He argues that because the texts on ta'zir are general, the minimum of that general (40) applies. Abu Yusuf, on the other hand, analogizes ta'zir to the punishment of a free person (80 lashes), considering them the original subjects of law. He then decreases by 5 (to 75) based on a report from Ali (RA). Some narrations say decrease by one lash (to 79). The author then cites al-Hawi al-Qudsi where Abu Yusuf explicitly sets the maximum at 39 for a slave and 75 for a free person, and that is the relied-upon view. The text notes that Zufar also says decrease by one from the free person's limit (to 79) based on qiyas, but the more correct view is Abu Yusuf's. Finally, Fath al-Qadir clarifies that these numbers apply only when the judge chooses flogging; otherwise, ta'zir may be by other means. The mufta bihi position is that the maximum for a slave is 39 and for a free person 75 lashes.

Key Terms
التعزير (al-ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for offenses that do not have a fixed hadd punishment or for which the hadd conditions are not met.
حد العبيد (hadd al-'abid): The fixed punishment for a slave for slander (qadhf) which is 40 lashes.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known and authoritative transmission from the founding imams, considered the primary source of fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is the maximum number of lashes in ta'zir for a free person?
A) 40 lashes
B) 75 lashes
C) 80 lashes
D) 39 lashes

Key Takeaway
The maximum ta'zir lashes in the Hanafi school are 39 for a slave and 75 for a free person, based on Abu Yusuf's view, which is the mufta bihi.

Minimum Ta'zir Lashes: Three or Discretionary?
States the minimum number of lashes in ta'zir and discusses disagreement on whether less suffices.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the minimum number of ta'zir lashes and explain the rationale of the later mashayikh.

Core Idea
The minimum ta'zir lashes is not fixed at three if the judge finds that fewer achieve deterrence.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a key difference within the Hanafi school about the minimum number of lashes in ta'zir punishment. While the text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that the minimum is three, the commentator Ibn Nujaym explains that later authorities (the mashayikh) held a more flexible view based on the purpose of deterrence. Understanding this difference is essential for correctly applying ta'zir in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling and its source
Note that the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states the minimum is three lashes, and al-Quduri is cited as holding this view.
This is the initial position presented in the text.
2
Understand al-Quduri's reasoning
Al-Quduri believed that fewer than three lashes cannot achieve the deterrent effect (zajr).
This reasoning is based on a fixed notion of deterrence.
3
Recognize the mashayikh's objection
The mashayikh argue that deterrence varies with individuals, so the number should be left to the judge's discretion. They reject a fixed minimum.
This view relies on the purpose of ta'zir rather than a numerical standard.
4
Determine the preferred view
The commentator indicates that the mashayikh's view is the relied-upone one, allowing the judge to give fewer than three if he deems it sufficient.
The practical outcome: the judge's estimation is paramount.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وأقله ثلاثة) أي أقل التعزير بالضرب ثلاثة أسواط وهكذا ذكر القدوري فكأنه یری أن ما دونها لا يقع به الزجر وليس كذلك، بل يختلف ذلك باختلاف الأشخاص فلا معنى لتقديره مع حصول المقصود بدونه فيكون مفوضاً إلى رأي القاضي يقيمه بقدر ما يرى المصلحة فيه على ما بينا تفاصيله وعليه مشايخنا ؛ كذا في التبيين والحاصل أن على ما في المختصر لو علم القاضي أن الزجر يحصل بسوط لا يكتفى به بل لا بد من الثلاثة وعلى قول المشايخ يكتفى به اهـ.
His statement: 'And its minimum is three' means the minimum of ta'zir by flogging is three lashes. Thus al-Quduri mentioned it, as if he thought that what is less than that does not achieve deterrence. But it is not so; rather, that varies with persons, so there is no meaning to estimating it when the purpose is achieved without it. Therefore, it is delegated to the opinion of the judge; he implements it according to what he sees as beneficial in it, as we have detailed. And upon that are our mashayikh. Likewise in al-Tabyin. The conclusion based on al-Mukhtasar is: if the judge knows that deterrence is achieved with one lash, he is not satisfied with it; rather, three are necessary. According to the opinion of the mashayikh, he is satisfied with it.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage discusses the minimum number of lashes in ta'zir. The text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states 'and its minimum is three.' The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) explains that al-Quduri held this view, believing that fewer than three lashes do not achieve the deterrent effect. However, the mashayikh (later scholars) disagree, stating that the minimum is not fixed; rather, it depends on the individual and the circumstances. If one lash suffices to deter, that is acceptable. The judge's discretion determines the appropriate number. The commentator notes a difference between al-Mukhtasar, which insists on three even if one lash would work, and the mashayikh who allow less. The author seems to favor the mashayikh's view, but the text presents both.

Key Terms
المشايخ (al-mashayikh): Later Hanafi scholars, especially those of the Bukhara school, who often gave more flexible rulings based on 'urf and maslaha.
الزجر (al-zajr): Deterrence; the purpose of ta'zir is to prevent future misconduct.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Flogging
B) Deterrence
C) Punishment
D) Discretion

Key Takeaway
The minimum ta'zir lashes is not fixed at three if the judge finds that fewer lashes achieve deterrence.

Combining Imprisonment with Flogging in Ta'zir
Commentary on combining imprisonment with flogging in ta'zir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining imprisonment with flogging in ta'zir and identify the conditions under which the judge may apply this combination.

Core Idea
Ta'zir aims at reform; each punishment alone is valid, so combining them is permissible.

This lesson examines a ruling from the Hanafi tradition: a judge may imprison a ta'zir offender even after flogging has been administered. We will explore the rationale—the discretionary nature of ta'zir for reform—and the practical scope of imprisonment options, including imprisonment in the offender's house or a designated prison.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is combining imprisonment with flogging in a ta'zir punishment. The ruling stated is 'valid' (جاز), meaning it is legally permissible and effective.
2
Understand the rationale for permissibility
The text explains that ta'zir is for reform, and the Law has generally allowed imprisonment alone or flogging alone. Therefore, adding one to the other is also allowed.
The mashru'iyyah (legitimacy) of each punishment individually supports combining them.
3
Note the distinction from hadd and ta'zir on suspicion
The passage notes that ta'zir based on suspicion (before proof) is not prescribed, unlike the case of hadd. This underscores that ta'zir requires established proof.
This distinction avoids abuse of discretionary punishment.
4
Recognize the scope of imprisonment
The term 'imprisonment' is absolute, covering both confinement in the offender's home or in a designated prison, as per al-Hawi al-Qudsi.
The judge chooses based on what is effective for reform.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وصح حبسه بعد الضرب أي جاز للحاكم أن يحبس العاصي بعد الضرب فيجمع بين حبسه وضربه لأنه صلح تعزيراً وقد ورد به الشرع في الجملة حتى جاز أن يكتفى به فجاز أن يضم إليه، ولهذا لم يشرع في التعزير بالتهمة قبل ثبوته كما شرع في الحد لأنه من التعزير . أطلق في الحبس فشمل الحبس في البيت والسجن . قال في الحاوي القدسي : وقد يكون التعزير بالحبس في بيته أو في السجن اهـ.
His statement: 'And his imprisonment after flogging is valid' means it is permissible for the judge to imprison the wrongdoer after flogging, thus combining imprisonment and flogging, because it is reform as ta'zir, and the Law has generally permitted it to the extent that it is permissible to suffice with it (imprisonment alone), so it is permissible to add it (to flogging). For this reason, ta'zir based on suspicion is not prescribed before it is established, as it is prescribed in hadd, because it is a type of ta'zir. The statement is absolute regarding imprisonment, so it includes imprisonment in the house and in prison. Al-Hawi al-Qudsi said: Ta'zir may be by imprisonment in his house or in prison.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage explains that a judge may combine imprisonment with flogging in a ta'zir punishment. The commentator clarifies that the rule of the matn 'his imprisonment after flogging is valid' means the judge has the option to imprison the offender after the flogging. This is permissible because ta'zir aims at reform, and the Shari'ah has generally allowed imprisonment as a standalone punishment; therefore, it can be added to flogging. The commentator also notes a distinction: ta'zir based on mere suspicion is not allowed before proof, whereas hadd can be prescribed on suspicion? Actually, the text says 'for this reason, ta'zir based on suspicion is not prescribed before it is established as it is prescribed in hadd' — meaning in hadd, punishment can be established on suspicion? That seems contradictory. More likely: 'as it is prescribed in hadd' means that in hadd, the punishment is not based on suspicion either; rather, it is similar. The text then notes that imprisonment can be in the offender's house or in prison, citing al-Hawi al-Qudsi.

Key Terms
الحبس (al-habs): Imprisonment; a form of ta'zir punishment.
التعزير بالتهمة (al-ta'zir bi al-tuhma): Discretionary punishment based on suspicion before the crime is proven.
التعزير (al-ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for offenses without fixed hadd or kaffarah, aimed at reform.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Severity Order of Flogging and Liability for Death in Punishment
Ranks punishments by severity and rules on death liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy of flogging severity and explain the rule of hagar (no liability) when death occurs during hadd or ta'zir, including the husband exception.

Core Idea
Ta'zir flogging is the most severe in quality, and death during lawful punishment is without blood-money.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq combines two key rulings from the Hanafi school: the relative severity of different flogging punishments, and the legal consequence if the punished person dies. Understanding these points is essential for correctly applying hudud and ta'zir, and for distinguishing between state-administered justice and a husband's disciplinary authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hierarchy of flogging severity
Read the text to find the order: ta'zir is the severest, then hadd of zina, then hadd of drinking, then hadd of qadhf. Note the reasoning: ta'zir has a lower number of lashes but greater force and concentration.
The text contrasts ta'zir with hadd: the number is reduced but quality is intensified to maintain deterrence.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on ta'zir technique
Examine the conflicting reports: some narrations say ta'zir lashes are concentrated on one limb, others say they are distributed. The resolution: concentration applies when ta'zir is at its maximum (39 lashes), distribution when it is less.
Al-Tabyin and Ghayat al-Bayan explain that there is no real contradiction; the difference is contextual.
3
Understand the justification for each hadd's rank
Hadd of zina comes before drinking because it is established by the Quran and is a graver crime (involving stoning). Hadd of drinking comes before qadhf because its cause (drinking) is certain, whereas qadhf's cause is uncertain (the accuser may be truthful).
This ranking is based on the proof (dalil) and the nature of the offense.
4
Grasp the rule of hagar (blood wasted) for death during punishment
The text states that if a person dies while being flogged for hadd or ta'zir, no diyah or qisas is due. The reason: the punishment is carried out by the command of the Lawgiver, and the administrator is not liable, just as a cupper is not liable for unintended harm.
The exception: a husband who disciplines his wife and causes death may be liable because his authority is not state-sanctioned punishment.
5
Apply the rule to a scenario
Consider a case: a thief dies during hadd of amputation (related but flogging discussed). Or a husband beats his wife for not adorning and she dies. Differentiate based on the principle: state punishment is hagar, husband's discipline may incur liability.
The husband's ta'zir is not considered 'punishment' in the same sense; it is a right of the husband with limitations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشد الضرب التعزير ثم حد الزنا ثم الشرب ثم القذف ومن حد أو عزر فمات فدمه هدر بخلاف الزوج إذا عزر زوجته لترك الزينة والإجابة إذا دعاها إلى فراشه وترك قوله : (وأشد الضرب التعزير لأنه جرى التخفيف فيه من حيث العدد فلا يخفف من حيث الوصف كيلا يؤدي إلى فوات المقصود. ولم يذكر المصنف أنه يفرق على الأعضاء كضرب الحدود لأنه لا يفرق كما في الهداية وإليه يشير إطلاق الأشدية الشاملة لقوته وجمعه في عضو واحد، وفي حدود الأصل يفرق التعزير على الأعضاء وفي أشربة الأصل يضرب التعزير في موضع واحد قال في التبيين وليس في المسألة اختلاف الرواية وإنما اختلف الجواب لاختلاف الموضوع، فموضوع الأول إذا بلغ بالتعزير أقصاه، وموضوع الثاني إذا لم يبلغ ا هـ . وهكذا في المجتبى وفي فتح القدير، وأثبت الاختلاف في غاية البيان معزياً إلى الأسبيجابي فقال بعضهم : الشدة هو الجمع فتجمع الأسواط في عضو واحد ولا يفرق على الأعضاء بخلاف سائر الحدود. وقال بعضهم : لا بل شدته في الضرب لا في الجمع اهـ. قالوا: ويتقي المواضع التي تتقى في الحدود. قال في المجتبى : ويضرب الظهر والألية. قالوا : ويبلغ في التعزير غايته وهو تسعة وثلاثون سوطاً فيما إذا أصاب من الأجنبية كل محرم غير الجماع، وفيما إذا أخذ السارق بعد ما جمع المتاع قبل الإخراج، وفيما إذا شتمه بجنس يجب به حد القذف كقوله للعبد أو الذمي يا زاني. وأشار بالأشدية إلى أنه يجرد من ثيابه. قال في غاية البيان ويجرد في سائر الحدود إلا في حد القذف فإنه يضرب وعليه ثيابه كما قدمناه. ويخالفه ما في فتاوى قاضيخان يضرب للتعزير قائماً عليه ثيابه وينزع الفرو والحشو ولا يمد في التعزير .اهـ. والظاهر الأول لتصريح المبسوط به وإلى أنه لو اجتمع التعزير مع الحدود قدم التعزير في الاستيفاء لتمحضه حقاً للعبد؛ كذا في الظهيرية قوله : (ثم حد الزنا) لأنه ثابت بالكتاب وحد الشرب ثابت بقول الصحابة رضي الله عنهم ولأنه أعظم جناية حتى شرع فيه الرجم قوله : (ثم الشرب ثم القذف) يعني حد الشرب يلي حد الزنا في شدة الضرب لما قدمناه وحد القذف أدنى الكل وإن كان ثابتاً بالكتاب إلا أن سببه محتمل لاحتمال كونه صادقاً وسبب حد الشرب متيقن به وهو الشرب والمراد أن الشرب متيقن السببية للحد لا متيقن الثبوت لأنه بالبينة أو الإقرار وهما لا يوجبان اليقين قوله : (ومن حد أو عزر فمات فدمه هدر لأنه فعل ما فعل بأمر الشارع وفعل المأمور لا يتقيد بشرط السلامة كالفصاد والبزاغ . قال في ضياء الحلوم : ذهب دمه هدراً أي باطلاً.
And the severest flogging is ta'zir, then the hadd of zina, then [the hadd of] drinking, then [the hadd of] qadhf. And whoever is punished by hadd or ta'zir and dies, his blood is considered of no account (hajar), unlike the husband if he disciplines his wife for neglecting adornment and responding when he calls her to his bed, and his statement: (And the severest flogging is ta'zir) because leniency was applied to it in terms of number, so it is not mitigated in terms of quality, lest the purpose be lost. The author did not mention that it is distributed over the limbs like the flogging of hadd, because it is not distributed, as mentioned in al-Hidayah, and that is indicated by the absolute nature of severity including its force and its concentration on one limb. In Hudud al-Asl, ta'zir is distributed over the limbs, and in Ashribat al-Asl, ta'zir flogging is on one spot. Al-Tabyin said: There is no disagreement in the narration; rather, the answer differs due to different contexts. The first is when the ta'zir reaches its maximum, the second when it has not reached its maximum. Thus in al-Mujtaba and Fath al-Qadir. And the dispute is affirmed in Ghayat al-Bayan attributed to al-Asbajabi. Some said: Severity means concentration, so the lashes are gathered on one limb unlike other hadd punishments. Others said: Rather, its severity is in the force of the blow, not in concentration. They said: He avoids the parts that are avoided in hadd. Al-Mujtaba said: He strikes the back and the buttocks. They said: Ta'zir reaches its maximum (39 lashes) in cases where he touches a foreign woman in every prohibited manner except intercourse, and when the thief takes the goods before taking them out, and when he insults someone with a type that requires hadd for qadhf, like saying to a slave or a dhimmi 'O fornicator.' And the expression of severity indicates that the offender is stripped of his clothes. Ghayat al-Bayan said: He is stripped in all hadd punishments except hadd for qadhf, as we mentioned. This is contradicted by what is in Fatawa Qadikhan: He is flogged for ta'zir standing, with his clothes on, and the fur and padding are removed, and he is not stretched in ta'zir. The apparent view is the first due to the explicit statement of al-Mabsut. And it is stated that if ta'zir and hadd are combined, ta'zir is given precedence in execution because it is purely a right of the servant. Likewise in al-Zahiriyyah. His statement: (Then the hadd of zina) because it is established by the Book, and the hadd of drinking is established by the saying of the Companions, and because it is the greatest crime, as stoning is prescribed in it. His statement: (Then drinking, then qadhf) means the hadd of drinking follows the hadd of zina in severity of flogging as we mentioned, and the hadd of qadhf is the least of all, even though it is established by the Book, but its cause is subject to the possibility that the accuser may be truthful, while the cause of the hadd of drinking is certain being drinking. And the intended meaning is that drinking is certain as a cause for the hadd, not certain in establishment, because it is by evidence or confession, which do not bring certainty. His statement: (And whoever is punished by hadd or ta'zir and dies, his blood is of no account) because he did what he did by the command of the Lawgiver, and the commanded act is not restricted by a condition of safety, like cupping and leeching. In Diya' al-Huloom: His blood is wasted, i.e., without compensation.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage covers two main rulings: (1) the order of severity in flogging among different punishments, and (2) the ruling if the punished person dies. The commentator explains that ta'zir flogging is the most severe because its number is less (only up to 39), so to achieve deterrence, the blows are harder and concentrated. There is a dispute whether the lashes in ta'zir should be concentrated on one spot or distributed. According to al-Hidayah, they are not distributed, but al-Asl has conflicting reports; the resolution is that distribution occurs when ta'zir reaches its maximum, and concentration when it does not. The severity also implies stripping the offender of his clothes, though there is difference with Fatawa Qadikhan. The order of severity is: ta'zir, then hadd of zina (because it is from the Quran), then hadd of drinking (from Companion consensus), then hadd of qadhf (from Quran but its cause is uncertain as the accuser might be truthful). Then the text states that if someone dies during a hadd or ta'zir punishment, his blood is of no account because the punishment was administered by legal authority, analogous to medical procedures like cupping. The exception is a husband disciplining his wife—if she dies, he may be liable because he is not a state authority. This husband exception is referenced but not elaborated in the extracted text.

Key Terms
هدر (hajar): Legally of no consequence; the blood-money is not mandatory.
الجمع (al-jam'): Concentration of flogging lashes on one limb, as opposed to distributing over the body.
التمحض (al-tamahhud): Being purely a right of the servant (individual right), as opposed to a right of Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the legal consequence if a person dies while being flogged for a valid ta'zir punishment?
A) The executor must pay diyah
B) The blood is hagar (no compensation)
C) The case goes to qisas
D) The punishment is invalidated

Key Takeaway
Ta'zir flogging is the most severe in quality due to force and concentration, and death during lawful punishment is hagar except for a husband's discipline.
