واحترز بقوله قدر» عشرة دراهم عن سرقة ما دونها. وأطلق في الدراهم فانصرفت إلى المعهودة وهي أن تكون العشرة منها وزن سبعة مثاقيل كما في الزكاة. واحترز بالمضروبة عما إذا سرق تبراً وزنه عشرة دراهم أو متاعاً قيمته عشرة دراهم غير مضروبة فإنه لا قطع فيه على الصحيح بخلاف المهر. والفرق أن الحد يدرأ بالشبهة فيتعلق بالكامل، والمهر يثبت مع الشبهة مع أن قوله مضروبة تأكيد وإيضاح وإلا فالدرهم اسم للمضروب، وأما غير المضروب فلا يسمى درهماً كما في المغرب، فلو سرق نصف دينار قيمته النصاب قطع عندنا ، ولو سرق ديناراً قيمته أقل من النصاب لا يقطع وتعتبر قيمة النصاب يوم السرقة ويوم القطع، فلو كانت قيمته يوم السرقة عشرة فانتقص بعد ذلك إن كان نقصان القيمة لنقصان العين يقطع ، وإن كان لنقصان السعر لا يقطع في ظاهر الرواية. ولو سرق ثوباً قيمته عشرة دراهم فأخذه المالك . في بلد آخر وقيمة الثوب ثمة ثمانية دراهم دريء عنه القطع، وإذا وجب تقويم المسروق بعشرة دراهم يقوم بأعز النقود أو بنقد البلد الذي يروج بين الناس في الغالب، فالأول رواية الحسن عن الإمام، والثاني رواية أبي يوسف عنه . ولا يقطع السارق بتقويم الواحد بل لا بد من تقويم رجلين عدلين لهما معرفة بالقيمة لأنه من باب الحدود فلا يثبت إلا بما ثبت به السرقة فلا قطع . عند اختلاف المقومين كما في الظهيرية وأطلق في قدر النصاب فشمل ما إذا كان المسروق منه واحداً أو أكثر ، فلو سرق واحد نصاباً من جماعة قطع، ولو سرق اثنان نصاباً من واحد لا قطع عليهما، فالعبرة للنصاب في حق السارق لا المسروق منه بشرط أن يكون الحرز واحداً، فلو سرق نصاباً من منزلين مختلفين فلا قطع، والبيوت من دار واحدة بمنزلة بيت واحد حتى لو سرق من عشرة أنفس في دار كل واحد في بيت على حدة من كل واحد منهم درهماً قطع بخلاف ما إذا كانت الدار عظيمة وفيها حجر كما في البدائع. وخرج باشتراط النصاب ما إذا سرق ثوباً قيمته تسعة دراهم فوضعه على باب الدار ثم دخل فأخذ ثوباً آخر يساوي تسعة دراهم فأخرجه عليه لم يقطع لأنه لم يبلغ المأخوذ في كل واحد منهما نصاباً؛ كذا في البدائع. وأطلق في حرز مرتين فصاعداً إن تخلل بينهما اطلاع المالك فأصلح النقب أو أغلق الباب فالإخراج الثاني سرقة أخرى؛ كذا في السراج اهـ. أي فلا يجب القطع إن لم يكن كل واحد نصاباً. ومقتضاه أنه إذا لم
And by his saying 'the value of ten dirhams' he distinguishes from theft of less than that. And he made 'dirhams' absolute, so it refers to the customary dirhams which are that ten of them weigh seven mithqals as in zakat. And by 'minted' he distinguishes from when he steals uncoined bullion weighing ten dirhams or goods worth ten dirhams but not minted, for there is no cutting in that according to the correct view, unlike the case of mahr. The difference is that the hadd is averted by doubt, so it attaches to the complete, while mahr is established despite doubt. And his saying 'minted' is an emphasis and clarification, for otherwise dirham is a name for the minted; as for unminted, it is not called dirham as in al-Mughrib. If he steals half a dinar worth the nisab, cutting applies in our school; if he steals a dinar worth less than the nisab, he is not cut off. And the value of the nisab is considered on the day of theft and on the day of cutting. If its value on the day of theft was ten, then it decreased afterwards, if the decrease is due to a defect in the object, he is cut; if due to a fall in market price, he is not cut according to the apparent narration. And if he steals a garment worth ten dirhams, then the owner takes it in another country where the garment's value is eight dirhams, the cutting is averted. And when it is necessary to evaluate the stolen property at ten dirhams, it is evaluated by the strongest currency or by the currency of the country that generally circulates among people; the first is the narration of Hasan from the Imam, the second is the narration of Abu Yusuf from him. And the thief is not cut on the evaluation of a single person, but rather two just men who have knowledge of value are required, because it is from the category of hadd punishments, so it is only established by such evidence as the theft itself; so there is no cutting when the valuers differ, as in al-Zahiriyya. And he made the nisab absolute, so it includes whether the victim is one or more. If one person steals a nisab from a group, he is cut; if two persons steal a nisab from one person, there is no cutting upon them. The consideration is the nisab in relation to the thief, not the victim, provided the guard (hirz) is one. If he steals a nisab from two different houses, there is no cutting. The rooms in one house are like one room, so if he steals from ten persons in a house, each in a separate room, one dirham from each, he is cut, contrary to if the house is large and has separate compartments, as in al-Badai'. And by the condition of nisab, if he steals a garment worth nine dirhams and places it at the door, then enters and takes another garment worth nine dirhams and takes it out, there is no cutting because the taken amount in each instance did not reach a nisab; as in al-Badai'. And he made it absolute regarding a guard: if he enters a guard twice or more, and between them the owner becomes aware and fixes the hole or closes the door, the second removal is another theft; as in al-Siraj. So there is no cutting unless each is a nisab. The implication is that if he did not...
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage details the condition of nisab (minimum value) for the application of the hadd of cutting. The nisab is ten dirhams, and these dirhams must be minted (i.e., coined currency). If someone steals uncoined gold or silver bullion weighing the equivalent of ten dirhams, or goods worth that value, the hadd does not apply according to the correct view, because the text specifies 'dirhams' which are minted by definition. However, if one steals half a dinar (a gold coin) worth ten dirhams, cutting applies because its value reaches the nisab. The value is checked both at the time of theft and at the time of cutting. If the value drops due to a defect in the object (e.g., the stolen item deteriorates), cutting still applies; but if the drop is due to a fall in market price (s'r), then cutting does not apply in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya). If the stolen goods are recovered in another country where their value is less than ten dirhams, cutting is averted. The evaluation of the stolen property must be done by two just experts; the thief is not cut on the opinion of a single valuer. The passage also discusses multiple thieves and multiple victims: If one thief steals a total nisab from multiple victims, he is cut. But if two thieves together steal a nisab from one victim, neither is cut, because the nisab is considered per thief. However, if the theft is from a single guarded place (hirz) that belongs to multiple owners, such as rooms in one house, the thief is cut if the total taken reaches the nisab. If the theft involves taking from separate hirz (different houses), no cutting for the total. Also, if the thief takes less than a nisab in one act, even if he later takes more from the same hirz after the owner becomes aware and repairs the breach, each act is considered separate and no cutting unless each act independently reaches the nisab.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The minimum value of stolen goods required for the hadd penalty: ten minted dirhams or their equivalent in gold or goods.
مضروبة (madruba): Minted coins; coins that have been struck and are legal tender, as opposed to bullion or raw metal.
تقويم (taqwim): Evaluation or appraisal of the stolen goods to determine if they reach the nisab; must be done by two just experts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a thief steals a garment worth ten dirhams on Monday, but by the time of the court hearing on Friday the market price drops so the garment is worth only nine dirhams, does the hadd of cutting apply?
A) Yes, because the value at theft was ten dirhams.
B) No, because the value at cutting is below the nisab.
C) Yes, because the drop is due to market price, not a defect in the garment.
D) No, because the nisab must be maintained throughout the process.

Key Takeaway
The hadd of cutting requires strict conditions: the stolen property must be ten minted dirhams or equivalent, with valuation by two just experts, and the nisab is considered per thief, not per victim.

Conditions of Secrecy and Nisab for Theft Hadd
Examines the requirement of secrecy and the nisab for the hadd of theft

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for the hadd of theft, explain the dispute on the secrecy criterion, and identify the correct nisab as ten minted dirhams.

Core Idea
The hadd of theft depends on the thief's belief in secrecy and requires ten minted dirhams.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq unpacks two essential conditions for applying the hadd of theft: secrecy (khafiyya) and the minimum value (nisab). Understanding these conditions is critical because the hadd is a severe penalty that is repelled by doubts. The commentator navigates an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether secrecy is judged by the thief's perception or the victim's knowledge, and clarifies that the stolen item must be minted silver coins, not raw metal or goods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions discussed
The passage addresses two distinct conditions for the hadd of theft: secrecy of the taking and the nisab of ten minted dirhams. Recognize that these are separate rulings with separate proofs.
Secrecy is about the act of taking; nisab is about the value of the stolen item.
2
Analyze the four scenarios of secrecy
The text presents four logical combinations of the thief's and victim's knowledge. Map them: (1) both know → no cut; (2) neither knows → cut; (3) victim knows, thief unaware → cut according to the relied-upon view; (4) thief thinks victim knows but victim doesn't → dispute between al-Tabyin (no cut) and al-Khulasa et al. (cut).
The relied-upon position (al-Khulasa, al-Muhit, al-Dhakhira) favors the thief's belief.
3
Understand the nisab requirement
The nisab for theft is ten dirhams of minted silver. The text emphasizes that the dirhams must be minted (madriba); uncoined silver (tibr) or goods of equivalent value do not trigger the hadd. Also note the weight standard: ten dirhams = seven mithqals, as in zakat.
The rationale: hadd is repelled by doubt, so it attaches only to the perfect (kamil) form of property.
4
Examine the talil (causal reasoning)
The commentator explains the difference between hadd and mahr: hadd is repelled by doubt, so it requires perfection (minted dirhams), while mahr is established despite doubt. This is a causal explanation (talil) justifying why uncoined silver does not suffice.
The argument uses the maxim 'al-hadd yudra'u bi al-shubha' (the hadd is repelled by doubts).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قطع به للاكتفاء بالخفية الأولى. ولم يبين المصنف أن المعتبر كونها خفية على زعم السارق أو المسروق منه فهي رباعية، فلو كان السارق يعلم أن صاحب الدار يعلم بدخوله وعلم به صاحب الدار أيضاً فلا قطع أو لم يعلما فيقطع اتفاقاً، أو كان صاحب الدار يعلم بدخوله والسارق لا يعلم أنه يعلم فإنه يقطع اكتفاء بكونها خفية في زعم السارق، وإن كان على عكسه بأن زعم اللص بأن صاحب الدار علم به وصاحب الدار لم يعلم ففي التبيين لا يقطع لأنه جهر. وفي الخلاصة والمحيط والذخيرة أنه يقطع اكتفاء بكونها خفية في زعم أيهما كان واحترز بقوله قدر» عشرة دراهم عن سرقـ رقة ما دونها. وأطلق في الدراهم فانصرفت إلى المعهودة وهي أن تكون العشرة منها وزن سبعة مثاقيل كما في الزكاة. أحدها واحترز بالمضروبة عما إذا سرق تبراً وزنه عشرة دراهم أو متاعاً قيمته عشرة دراهم غير مضروبة فإنه لا قطع فيه على الصحيح بخلاف المهر. والفرق أن الحد يدرأ بالشبهة فيتعلق بالكامل، والمهر يثبت مع الشبهة مع أن قوله مضروبة تأكيد وإيضاح وإلا فالدرهم اسم للمضروب، وأما غير المضروب فلا يسمى درهماً كما في المغرب
It cuts (the hand) due to sufficing with the first secrecy. The author did not clarify whether the consideration is that it be secret according to the claim of the thief or the victim, so it is four-fold. If the thief knows that the owner of the house knows of his entry and the owner also knows, then no cutting; or if neither knows, then cutting by agreement. Or if the owner knows of his entry and the thief does not know that he knows, then he is cut, deeming it secret according to the thief's claim. And if the opposite, that the thief claims that the owner knew and the owner did not know, then in al-Tabyin there is no cutting because it is open. And in al-Khulasa, al-Muhit, and al-Dhakhira, he is cut, deeming it secret according to the claim of either. And he guarded by his saying "ten dirhams" against stealing a rag (riqqa) less than that. And he left general in dirhams, so they refer to the well-known ones, which are that ten of them weigh seven mithqals as in zakat. One of them: and he guarded by "minted" against the case where he steals uncoined silver weighing ten dirhams or goods worth ten dirhams unminted, for there is no cutting in that according to the correct view, unlike the bridal gift. The difference is that the hadd is repelled by doubt, so it attaches to the perfect, while the bridal gift is established despite doubt. Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the conditions for the hadd of theft. It first discusses the requirement of secrecy (khafiyya): the theft must be carried out in a manner that the victim is unaware. There is a dispute among Hanafi scholars as to whether the criterion is the thief's belief or the victim's knowledge. The author cites al-Tabyin, which holds that if the victim knows, the theft is considered open (jahr) and no cutting applies. However, the relied-upon position in al-Khulasa, al-Muhit, and al-Dhakhira is that it suffices that the thief believes it to be secret, even if the victim knows. The passage then addresses the nisab: it must be ten dirhams of minted silver. Unminted silver (tibr) or goods worth ten dirhams do not trigger the cut. The author notes the difference between hadd and mahr: hadd is repelled by doubt, so it requires perfection, whereas mahr is established even with doubt. The term 'minted' is an emphasis because dirham inherently means a coined coin.

Key Terms
خفية (khafiyya): Secrecy: the theft must be done in a way that the victim is unaware of the taking at the time it occurs.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum threshold of value for the hadd of theft: ten dirhams of minted silver.
درهم مضروب (dirham madhrib): A minted coin made of silver, as opposed to raw silver (tibr) or unminted metal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a thief steals uncoined silver (tibr) worth 10 dirhams, is the hadd of cutting applied according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Yes, because it exceeds the nisab.
B) Yes, if he believes it is secret.
C) No, because it is not minted dirhams.
D) No, because the victim knew.

Key Takeaway
The hadd of theft requires the thief's belief in secrecy and a stolen item of ten minted dirhams; both conditions must be met exactly.

Timing of Nisab Evaluation: Theft and Judgment
Rule on nisab timing and value change

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that the nisab is evaluated at both the time of theft and the time of judgment, and distinguish between a value decrease due to a defect in the item vs. a market price drop.

Core Idea
The nisab must be met at both theft and judgment; a market drop averts the cut, but a defect drop does not.

In this lesson, we examine one of the key conditions for the hadd of theft: the value of the stolen property must reach the nisab at two specific times. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains how to handle changes in value, revealing a nuance that upholds justice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? (theft of an item whose value changes) What is the ruling? (cutting or no cutting)
2
Determine the timing of evaluation
The text states 'on the day of theft and the day of cutting.' Understand why both are needed.
3
Distinguish the cause of value change
If the value drops due to a defect in the item, the cut remains. If due to market price, the cut is averted. Identify the reasoning (talil).
This is a form of talil: the cause of the drop matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو سرق نصف دينار قيمته النصاب قطع عندنا ، ولو سرق ديناراً قيمته أقل من النصاب لا يقطع وتعتبر قيمة النصاب يوم السرقة ويوم القطع، فلو كانت قيمته يوم السرقة عشرة فانتقص بعد ذلك إن كان نقصان القيمة لنقصان العين يقطع ، وإن كان لنقصان السعر لا يقطع في ظاهر الرواية. ولو سرق ثوباً قيمته عشرة دراهم فأخذه المالك . في بلد آخر وقيمة الثوب ثمة ثمانية دراهم دريء عنه القطع، وإذا وجب تقويم المسروق بعشرة دراهم يقوم بأعز النقود أو بنقد البلد الذي يروج بين الناس في الغالب، فالأول رواية الحسن عن الإمام، والثاني رواية أبي يوسف عنه . ولا يقطع السارق بتقويم الواحد بل لا بد من تقويم رجلين عدلين لهما معرفة بالقيمة لأنه من باب الحدود فلا يثبت إلا بما ثبت به السرقة فلا قطع . عند اختلاف المقومين كما في الظهيرية وأطلق في قدر النصاب فشمل ما إذا كان المسروق منه واحداً أو أكثر ، فلو سرق واحد نصاباً من جماعة قطع، ولو سرق اثنان نصاباً من واحد لا قطع عليهما، فالعبرة للنصاب في حق السارق لا المسروق منه بشرط أن يكون الحرز واحداً، فلو سرق نصاباً من منزلين مختلفين فلا قطع، والبيوت من دار واحدة بمنزلة بيت واحد حتى لو سرق من عشرة أنفس في دار كل واحد في بيت على حدة من كل واحد منهم درهماً قطع بخلاف ما إذا كانت الدار عظيمة وفيها حجر كما في البدائع. وخرج باشتراط النصاب ما إذا سرق ثوباً قيمته تسعة دراهم فوضعه على باب الدار ثم دخل فأخذ ثوباً آخر يساوي تسعة دراهم فأخرجه عليه لم يقطع لأنه لم يبلغ المأخوذ في كل واحد منهما نصاباً ؛ كذا في البدائع. وأطلق في حرز مرتين فصاعداً إن تخلل بينهما اطلاع المالك فأصلح النقب أو أغلق الباب فالإخراج الثاني سرقة أخرى؛ كذا في السراج اهـ. أي فلا يجب القطع إن لم يكن كل واحد نصاباً. ومقتضاه أنه إذا لم يتخلل ذلك قطع وقد رأيته في الجوهرة صرح به فيتقيد ما ذكره المؤلف .به. قوله : (وفي القنية لو سرق المدفون الخ) ذكر المقدسي عند مسألة النباش أن ما في القنية ضعيف قوله : (وعليه ذكر في التجنيس الخ) أي على ما ذكر من ثبوت دلالة القصد لكن ظاهر عبارة التجنيس أنه لا يقطع وإن علم في الثوب. وفي الفتح عن المبسوط : سرق ثوباً لا يساوي عشرة مصرور عليه عشرة قال : يقطع إذا علم أن عليه ما لا بخلاف ما إذا لم يعلم .اهـ. ثم قال في الفتح : فالحاصل أنه يعتبر ظهور قصد المسروق فإن كان الظاهر قصد النصاب من المال قطع وإلا لا. وعلى هذا فمسألة العلم بالمصرور
If he steals half a dinar whose value is the nisab, it is cut in our view. If he steals a dinar whose value is less than the nisab, he is not cut. And the value of the nisab is considered on the day of theft and the day of cutting. If its value on the day of theft was ten and then decreased, if the decrease is due to a defect in the item, he is cut; if due to a fall in market price, he is not cut in the apparent narration. If he steals a cloth worth ten dirhams and the owner takes it in another country where its value is eight dirhams, the cutting is averted. When evaluation of the stolen item at ten dirhams is required, it is evaluated by the most precious currency or by the currency of the country that is commonly circulated. The first is the narration of al-Hasan from the Imam (Abu Hanifa), and the second is the narration of Abu Yusuf from him. The thief is not cut by the evaluation of one person; rather, the evaluation of two just men who know values is necessary, because this is from the category of hudud, so it is not established except by what establishes the theft; thus no cutting when the valuers disagree, as in al-Dhahira. He was general in the amount of the nisab, so it includes whether the victim is one or more. If one steals a nisab from a group, he is cut. If two steal a nisab from one, there is no cutting on them. The consideration is the nisab in regard to the thief, not the victim, on condition that the place of safekeeping is one. If he steals a nisab from two different houses, no cutting. The rooms of one house are like one room, so if he steals from ten individuals in a house, each in a separate room, taking one dirham from each, he is cut, unlike if the house is large and has separate compartments as in al-Bada'i. By requiring the nisab, it excludes: if he steals a cloth worth nine dirhams, places it on the door of the house, then enters and takes another cloth worth nine dirhams and takes it out, he is not cut because the taken amount in each case did not reach the nisab—this is as in al-Bada'i. He was general about a place of safekeeping twice or more: if between them there is the owner's awareness and he repairs the hole or closes the door, the second removal is another theft—this is as in al-Siraj. That is, cutting is not required if each is not a nisab. Its implication is that if that (awareness) does not intervene, it is one theft, and I have seen that in al-Jawhara, he explicitly stated it, so what the author mentioned is restricted by this. His statement: (And in al-Quniya: if he steals buried property, etc.) al-Maqdisi mentioned in the issue of the grave-robber that what is in al-Quniya is weak. His statement: (And upon this, mentioned in al-Tajnisi, etc.) i.e., based on what was mentioned of establishing the indication of intent, but the apparent wording of al-Tajnisi is that he is not cut even if he knows (the dirham) is in the cloth. And in al-Fath from al-Mabsut: he stole a cloth worth less than ten, with ten tied on it. He said: he is cut if he knows that there is wealth on it, unlike if he does not know. Then in al-Fath he said: the conclusion is that the appearance of the intent of the stolen item is considered: if the apparent intent is the nisab of wealth, he is cut; otherwise no. And upon this, the issue of knowledge of the tied money.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the conditions for the hadd of theft. It first addresses the evaluation of the nisab: the value is considered both at the time of theft and at the time of judgment. If the value drops due to a defect in the item itself (not market fluctuation), the cutting is still applied. If the drop is due to market change, no cutting. The author then discusses the location of evaluation: if the stolen item is taken to another country where its value is lower, the cutting is averted. There is a dispute whether to evaluate by the most precious currency or the local currency; the first is from Hasan ibn Ziyad, the second from Abu Yusuf. The evaluation must be done by two just valuers; disagreement among them prevents the cutting. The passage then covers cases of multiple victims or multiple thieves: the nisab is considered per thief, not per victim. The place of safekeeping must be one; stealing from separate houses precludes cutting even if the total reaches the nisab. The example of two thefts from the same place with the owner's intervention in between shows that each theft is separate, so each must independently reach the nisab. Finally, the passage discusses intent (qasd): if a cloth has money tied to it and the thief knows, cutting applies; if he does not know, no cutting. The relied-upon principle is the appearance of intent: if the apparent intent is the nisab, cutting is applied.

Key Terms
تقويم (taqwim): Valuation: the assessment of the stolen item's worth to determine if it reaches the nisab.
نقصان العين (nuqsan al-'ayn): Decrease in value due to a physical defect in the item itself.
نقصان السعر (nuqsan al-si'r): Decrease in value due to market price fluctuation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a stolen item's value drops from 10 to 8 dirhams due to a market price decline, what is the ruling?
A) The thief is cut because the nisab was met at theft.
B) The thief is not cut because the value at judgment is below the nisab.
C) The thief is cut if he intended to steal the nisab.
D) The thief is not cut only if the item is not minted dirhams.

Key Takeaway
The nisab must be met at both the time of theft and the time of judgment; a market-driven drop below the nisab averts the hadd.

Currency for Valuation and the Requirement of Two Valuers
Rule on currency valuation and requirement of valuers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two narrations regarding the currency for evaluating the stolen item and state the Hanafi requirement of two just valuers.

Core Idea
Valuation is by the local common currency and must be performed by two just, knowledgeable valuers.

When determining the value of the stolen item, two questions arise: which currency to use, and who evaluates? The passage presents two narrations from Abu Hanifa—one using the most precious currency, the other using the local currency. It also clarifies that one valuer is insufficient for a hadd case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two narrations on currency
From the text: the first narration (Hasan ibn Ziyad) uses the most precious currency; the second (Abu Yusuf) uses the local common currency.
Both are from Abu Hanifa.
2
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view is Abu Yusuf's: evaluation by the local currency, as it is more practical.
This is consistent with the school's later preference.
3
State the requirement of two valuers
The text says 'the thief is not cut by the evaluation of one person; rather, the evaluation of two just men who know values is necessary'.
Disagreement between the two valuers prevents the cutting.

Nisab in Relation to Thief vs. Victim and Unity of Hirz
Rule on nisab allocation and hirz unity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the nisab is considered per thief (not per victim) and that the theft must be from a single hirz.

Core Idea
The nisab is calculated per thief, not per victim, and the theft must be from one secure location; multiple hirz block the hadd.

This lesson clarifies how the nisab is allocated when there are multiple victims or multiple thieves. It also emphasizes that the stolen property must come from a single place of safekeeping (hirz). The passage provides examples to illustrate these conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle: nisab per thief
The text says: 'If one steals a nisab from a group, he is cut. If two steal a nisab from one, there is no cutting on them.' Thus, the nisab is considered individually for each thief.
This is independent of the number of victims.
2
Apply the unity of hirz condition
If the stolen property comes from two different houses (hirz), even if total equals nisab, no cutting. The hirz must be one.
Exception: rooms in one house count as one hirz.
3
Understand the implication of multiple thefts from same hirz
If the thief steals from the same hirz in multiple trips without owner's awareness, each theft is separate; if each is less than nisab, no cut.
Owner's intervention (repairing hole, closing door) separates the thefts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو سرق نصف دينار قيمته النصاب قطع عندنا ، ولو سرق ديناراً قيمته أقل من النصاب لا يقطع وتعتبر قيمة النصاب يوم السرقة ويوم القطع، فلو كانت قيمته يوم السرقة عشرة فانتقص بعد ذلك إن كان نقصان القيمة لنقصان العين يقطع ، وإن كان لنقصان السعر لا يقطع في ظاهر الرواية. ولو سرق ثوباً قيمته عشرة دراهم فأخذه المالك . في بلد آخر وقيمة الثوب ثمة ثمانية دراهم دريء عنه القطع، وإذا وجب تقويم المسروق بعشرة دراهم يقوم بأعز النقود أو بنقد البلد الذي يروج بين الناس في الغالب، فالأول رواية الحسن عن الإمام، والثاني رواية أبي يوسف عنه . ولا يقطع السارق بتقويم الواحد بل لا بد من تقويم رجلين عدلين لهما معرفة بالقيمة لأنه من باب الحدود فلا يثبت إلا بما ثبت به السرقة فلا قطع . عند اختلاف المقومين كما في الظهيرية وأطلق في قدر النصاب فشمل ما إذا كان المسروق منه واحداً أو أكثر ، فلو سرق واحد نصاباً من جماعة قطع، ولو سرق اثنان نصاباً من واحد لا قطع عليهما، فالعبرة للنصاب في حق السارق لا المسروق منه بشرط أن يكون الحرز واحداً، فلو سرق نصاباً من منزلين مختلفين فلا قطع، والبيوت من دار واحدة بمنزلة بيت واحد حتى لو سرق من عشرة أنفس في دار كل واحد في بيت على حدة من كل واحد منهم درهماً قطع بخلاف ما إذا كانت الدار عظيمة وفيها حجر كما في البدائع. وخرج باشتراط النصاب ما إذا سرق ثوباً قيمته تسعة دراهم فوضعه على باب الدار ثم دخل فأخذ ثوباً آخر يساوي تسعة دراهم فأخرجه عليه لم يقطع لأنه لم يبلغ المأخوذ في كل واحد منهما نصاباً ؛ كذا في البدائع. وأطلق في حرز مرتين فصاعداً إن تخلل بينهما اطلاع المالك فأصلح النقب أو أغلق الباب فالإخراج الثاني سرقة أخرى؛ كذا في السراج اهـ. أي فلا يجب القطع إن لم يكن كل واحد نصاباً. ومقتضاه أنه إذا لم يتخلل ذلك قطع وقد رأيته في الجوهرة صرح به فيتقيد ما ذكره المؤلف .به. قوله : (وفي القنية لو سرق المدفون الخ) ذكر المقدسي عند مسألة النباش أن ما في القنية ضعيف قوله : (وعليه ذكر في التجنيس الخ) أي على ما ذكر من ثبوت دلالة القصد لكن ظاهر عبارة التجنيس أنه لا يقطع وإن علم في الثوب. وفي الفتح عن المبسوط : سرق ثوباً لا يساوي عشرة مصرور عليه عشرة قال : يقطع إذا علم أن عليه ما لا بخلاف ما إذا لم يعلم .اهـ. ثم قال في الفتح : فالحاصل أنه يعتبر ظهور قصد المسروق فإن كان الظاهر قصد النصاب من المال قطع وإلا لا. وعلى هذا فمسألة العلم بالمصرور
If he steals half a dinar whose value is the nisab, it is cut in our view. If he steals a dinar whose value is less than the nisab, he is not cut. And the value of the nisab is considered on the day of theft and the day of cutting. If its value on the day of theft was ten and then decreased, if the decrease is due to a defect in the item, he is cut; if due to a fall in market price, he is not cut in the apparent narration. If he steals a cloth worth ten dirhams and the owner takes it in another country where its value is eight dirhams, the cutting is averted. When evaluation of the stolen item at ten dirhams is required, it is evaluated by the most precious currency or by the currency of the country that is commonly circulated. The first is the narration of al-Hasan from the Imam (Abu Hanifa), and the second is the narration of Abu Yusuf from him. The thief is not cut by the evaluation of one person; rather, the evaluation of two just men who know values is necessary, because this is from the category of hudud, so it is not established except by what establishes the theft; thus no cutting when the valuers disagree, as in al-Dhahira. He was general in the amount of the nisab, so it includes whether the victim is one or more. If one steals a nisab from a group, he is cut. If two steal a nisab from one, there is no cutting on them. The consideration is the nisab in regard to the thief, not the victim, on condition that the place of safekeeping is one. If he steals a nisab from two different houses, no cutting. The rooms of one house are like one room, so if he steals from ten individuals in a house, each in a separate room, taking one dirham from each, he is cut, unlike if the house is large and has separate compartments as in al-Bada'i. By requiring the nisab, it excludes: if he steals a cloth worth nine dirhams, places it on the door of the house, then enters and takes another cloth worth nine dirhams and takes it out, he is not cut because the taken amount in each case did not reach the nisab—this is as in al-Bada'i. He was general about a place of safekeeping twice or more: if between them there is the owner's awareness and he repairs the hole or closes the door, the second removal is another theft—this is as in al-Siraj. That is, cutting is not required if each is not a nisab. Its implication is that if that (awareness) does not intervene, it is one theft, and I have seen that in al-Jawhara, he explicitly stated it, so what the author mentioned is restricted by this. His statement: (And in al-Quniya: if he steals buried property, etc.) al-Maqdisi mentioned in the issue of the grave-robber that what is in al-Quniya is weak. His statement: (And upon this, mentioned in al-Tajnisi, etc.) i.e., based on what was mentioned of establishing the indication of intent, but the apparent wording of al-Tajnisi is that he is not cut even if he knows (the dirham) is in the cloth. And in al-Fath from al-Mabsut: he stole a cloth worth less than ten, with ten tied on it. He said: he is cut if he knows that there is wealth on it, unlike if he does not know. Then in al-Fath he said: the conclusion is that the appearance of the intent of the stolen item is considered: if the apparent intent is the nisab of wealth, he is cut; otherwise no. And upon this, the issue of knowledge of the tied money.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the conditions for the hadd of theft. It first addresses the evaluation of the nisab: the value is considered both at the time of theft and at the time of judgment. If the value drops due to a defect in the item itself (not market fluctuation), the cutting is still applied. If the drop is due to market change, no cutting. The author then discusses the location of evaluation: if the stolen item is taken to another country where its value is lower, the cutting is averted. There is a dispute whether to evaluate by the most precious currency or the local currency; the first is from Hasan ibn Ziyad, the second from Abu Yusuf. The evaluation must be done by two just valuers; disagreement among them prevents the cutting. The passage then covers cases of multiple victims or multiple thieves: the nisab is considered per thief, not per victim. The place of safekeeping must be one; stealing from separate houses precludes cutting even if the total reaches the nisab. The example of two thefts from the same place with the owner's intervention in between shows that each theft is separate, so each must independently reach the nisab. Finally, the passage discusses intent (qasd): if a cloth has money tied to it and the thief knows, cutting applies; if he does not know, no cutting. The relied-upon principle is the appearance of intent: if the apparent intent is the nisab, cutting is applied.

Key Terms
حرز (hirz): A place of safekeeping: a location where property is stored securely.
النصاب في حق السارق (al-nisab fi haqq al-sariq): The nisab is considered in relation to the thief individually, not the victim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two thieves together steal 10 dirhams from one house. According to Hanafi law, what is the ruling?
A) Both are cut because the total is nisab.
B) Neither is cut because each must individually steal the nisab.
C) The one who took more than 5 dirhams is cut.
D) Both are cut because the hirz is one.

Key Takeaway
The nisab is calculated per thief, not per victim, and the theft must be from a single hirz.

Intent (Qasd) and Knowledge of Hidden Money
Rule on intent and hidden money

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the thief's intent (qasd) is assessed by the apparent nature of the stolen item, and determine whether cutting applies when money is hidden in a cloth.

Core Idea
The hadd depends on the apparent intent; if the item's appearance indicates nisab, cutting applies even if the thief claims ignorance.

The final part of the passage addresses a subtle point: what if a thief steals a cloth that has money tied inside it? The ruling depends on whether the thief knew about the money. Hanafi law considers the 'appearance of intent'—if the object's outward condition suggests the nisab, the hadd is applied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario: cloth with hidden money
The text discusses a cloth worth less than ten dirhams but with ten dirhams tied on it. The thief's knowledge is key.
2
Determine the ruling based on knowledge
If the thief knows there is money on the cloth, he is cut. If he does not know, he is not cut.
Know stands for certain knowledge (yaqin) or apparent indication.
3
Apply the principle of zahir al-qasd
The relied-upon position from al-Fath is that the appearance of intent is considered. If the cloth appears to have money (e.g., is rolled or tied), the thief is cut even if he claims he didn't know.
This avoids the thief's subjective claim defeating the hadd.

Source Text

Key Terms
قصد (qasd): Intent: the thief must intend to steal the nisab; assessed by appearance.
ظهور قصد المسروق (zuhoor qasd al-masrooq): The appearance of the intent of the stolen item; the outward sign that the item contains the nisab.
مصرور (masrur): Tied or bundled; a cloth with money tied on it.

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (al-Fath), what is the key factor in determining the intent of the thief?
A) The thief's confession of intent.
B) The apparent nature of the stolen item.
C) The victim's assessment of the thief's intention.
D) The value of the stolen item alone.

Key Takeaway
The thief's intent to steal the nisab is determined by the outward appearance of the stolen item; if the item appears to contain the nisab, cutting applies.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate

Conditions for the Hadd of Theft in Hanafi Fiqh
Conditions for hadd of theft, including thief capacity, hirz types, and intent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nine conditions required for the hadd of theft and apply them to determine whether a given scenario triggers the fixed punishment.

Core Idea
Nine conditions must be met before the hadd of theft applies; any missing condition averts the cutting of the hand.

This lesson examines the specific conditions that must be fulfilled for the hadd (fixed punishment) of theft to be applied in Hanafi law. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq details each requirement, from the nature of the stolen property to the capacity of the thief and the location of the theft. Understanding these conditions is essential because the hudud are averted by doubts, and each condition serves as a safeguard against wrongful punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall hukm and its rukn
Start by noting that the hadd for theft is the cutting of the right hand, and the rukn (pillar) is the actual taking (akhdh) of the property from the hirz. Without this act, no hadd.
The rukn is the taking itself; all else are conditions.
2
List the shurut (conditions) in order
From the passage, extract all conditions: mal mutaqawwim, owned by another, no shubha, thief not mute/blind, theft in dar al-Islam, intent to steal nisab, victim's valid hand, open removal (ikhraj zahir), healthy limbs (left hand and right foot). Confirm each from the text.
The author provides a comprehensive definition at the end that includes all these.
3
Understand the rationale (ta'lil) behind each condition
For each condition, ask why it is required. For example, the mute is excluded because he might claim a doubt if he could speak; the blind is excluded because he is ignorant of ownership; swallowing avoids open removal; etc.
The ta'lil helps in applying the rules to new cases.
4
Distinguish between the two types of hirz
Separate hirz bi-nafsihi (inherently secure places like houses) from hirz bi-ghayrihi (places made secure by a guardian, like mosques). Understand how the type affects the requirement of a guardian.
Mosques and roads are not hirz by themselves; they need a guardian.
5
Apply the conditions to a borderline case
Consider the case of swallowing a dinar inside the hirz. Identify which condition is missing (ikhraj zahir) and conclude that no hadd applies. Then note the guarantee (daman) for the destroyed property.
This illustrates how a single missing condition averts the hadd.

وقد استفيد من اشتراط النصاب اشتراط أن يكون المسروق مالاً متقوماً، ولا بد أن يكون مملوكاً لغيره فلا قطع في حصر المسجد وأستار الكعبة وإن كانت محرزة . ولا بد من انتفاء الشبهة ولم يذكرهما لما سيصرح به، ولا بد من كون السارق ليس بأخرس ولا أعمى لاحتمال أنه لو نطق ادعى شبهة والأعمى جاهل بمال غيره. وقوله «محرزة بمكان أو حافظ بيان لكون الحرز على قسمين : حرز بنفسه وهو كل بقعة معدة للإحراز ممنوع الدخول فيها إلا بإذن كالدور والحوانيت والخيم والخزائن والصناديق. وحرز بغيره وهو كل مكان غير معد للإحراز وفيه حافظ كالمساجد والطرق والصحراء وسيأتي بيانهما . وفي القنية : لو سرق المدفون في المفازة يقطع .اهـ. ولا بد أن تكون السرقة في دار العدل فلا يقطع في السرقة في دار الحرب ودار البغي فلو سرق بعض تجار المسلمين من البعض في دار الحرب ثم خرجوا إلى دار الإسلام فأخذ السارق لا يقطعه الإمام ؛ كذا في البدائع. ولا بد من ثبوت دلالة القصد إلى النصاب المأخوذ . وعليه ذكر في التجنيس من علامة النوازل : سرق ثوباً قيمته دون العشرة وعلى طرفه دينار مشدود لا يقطع . وذكر من علامة فتاوى سمرقند إذا سرق ثوباً لا يساوي عشرة وفيه دراهم مصرورة لا يقطع قال : وهذا إذا لم يكن الثوب وعاء للدراهم عادة، فإن كان يقطع لأن القصد فيه يقع على سرقة الدراهم ألا ترى أنه لو سرق كيساً فيه دراهم كثيرة يقطع وإن كان الكيس يساوي درهماً. ولا بد أن يكون للمسروق منه يد صحيحة فخرج السارق من السارق، ولا بد أن يخرجه ظاهراً حتى لو ابتلع ديناراً في الحرز وخرج لا يقطع، ولا ينتظر أن يتغوطه بل يضمن مثله لأنه استهلكه وهو سبب الضمان للحال فقد علمت مما ذكرناه أن تعريف المختصر قاصر، فلو قال المصنف هي أخذ مكلف ناطق بصير صاحب يد يسرى ورجل يمني صحيحتين عشرة دراهم جياد أو مقدارها مقصودة ظاهرة الإخراج خفية من صاحب يد صحيحة مما لا يتسارع إليه الفساد . من المال المعمول للغير من حرز بلا شبهة وتأويل في دار العدل» لكان أولى وقد علمت فوائد القيود . وفي الظهيرية وشرط أصحابنا لقطع اليد اليمني أن تكون اليد اليسرى والرجل اليمنى صحيحتين، وهكذا ذكره في المجتبى من الشروط . وفي التحقيق أن الأخذ المذكور هو ركنها .
And it is derived from the condition of the nisab the requirement that the stolen item be valuable property (mal mutaqawwim), and it must be owned by another; so no cutting for stealing a mat from a mosque or the curtains of the Ka'ba, even if they are in a secure place. And the absence of doubt (shubha) is required, and the author did not mention them because he will state them later. And the thief must not be mute or blind, because if he were to speak he might claim a doubt, and the blind person is ignorant of others' property. And his statement: 'safeguarded in a place or by a guardian' is an explanation that hirz is of two types: hirz by itself, which is every place designated for safekeeping, entry prohibited without permission, such as houses, shops, tents, vaults, and chests; and hirz by another, which is every place not designated for safekeeping but has a guardian, such as mosques, roads, and the desert, and their explanation will come. In al-Quniya: if he steals buried property in the desert, he is cut—end. And the theft must occur in the abode of justice (dar al-'adl), so no cutting for theft in dar al-harb or dar al-baghy. If some Muslim merchants steal from others in dar al-harb and then come to dar al-Islam and the thief is caught, the imam does not cut him—as in al-Bada'i. And the evidence of intent (qasd) towards the taken nisab must be established. Upon this, in al-Tajnisi from the signs of nawazil: he stole a cloth worth less than ten, and on its edge a dinar tied, he is not cut. And from the fatwas of Samarkand: if he steals a cloth not worth ten, and in it tied dirhams, he is not cut. He said: this if the cloth is not customarily a container for dirhams; if it is, he is cut because the intent falls on stealing the dirhams. Do you not see that if he steals a pouch containing many dirhams, he is cut even if the pouch is worth one dirham. And the victim must have a valid hand (yad sahiha), thus the thief from a thief is excluded. And he must take it out in an apparent manner; so if he swallows a dinar inside the hirz and exits, he is not cut, and we do not wait for him to pass it, rather he guarantees its like because he destroyed it and it is the cause of guarantee immediately. So you have known from what we have mentioned that the definition of the mukhtasar (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) is deficient. If the author had said: 'It is the taking by a legally responsible, speaking, seeing person, having a left hand and a right foot that are healthy, of ten good dirhams or their equivalent, intended, with apparent removal, secretly, from an owner with a valid hand, from property that does not quickly spoil, from property worked for others, from a place of safekeeping, without doubt or interpretation, in the abode of justice'—it would be better, and you have known the benefits of the restrictions. And in al-Dhahira: our companions have stipulated for cutting the right hand that the left hand and the right foot be healthy. Thus it is mentioned in al-Mujtaba among the conditions. And in verification, the aforementioned taking is its pillar (rukn).
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage completes the discussion of conditions for the hadd of theft by listing several additional requirements. First, the stolen property must be valuable (mal mutaqawwim) and owned by another, not public property like mosque mats. Second, there must be no doubt (shubha) that could avert the hadd; the author notes the matn omitted this. Third, the thief must be capable of speech and sight: a mute might claim a doubt if he could speak, and a blind person is ignorant of others' property. Fourth, the place of safekeeping (hirz) is detailed: either a place inherently secure (like a house) or a place made secure by a guardian (like a guarded mosque). Fifth, the theft must occur in dar al-Islam; cutting is not applied in dar al-harb or dar al-baghy. Sixth, the thief must intend to steal the nisab; the appearance of intent matters (e.g., a bag known to contain money). Seventh, the victim must have a valid ownership hand (yad sahiha), so stealing from a thief does not trigger the hadd. Eighth, the thief must physically remove the item from the hirz openly (not by swallowing). Ninth, the thief's limbs must be healthy: the left hand and right foot must be intact for the cutting of the right hand to be valid. The author concludes by suggesting a more comprehensive definition of theft that incorporates all these conditions.

Key Terms
حرز بنفسه (hirz bi-nafsihi): A place inherently secure for safekeeping, such as a house, shop, or locked container, where entry is restricted.
دار العدل (dar al-'adl): The abode of justice: a territory where Islamic law is applied, i.e., dar al-Islam.
شبهة (shubha): Doubt or ambiguity that can avert the hadd punishment, such as a claim of ownership or a contractual right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the hadd of theft not applied if a blind person steals from a house?
A) Because a blind person cannot commit theft.
B) Because a blind person is ignorant of others' property and may have a doubt.
C) Because a blind person cannot see the hirz.
D) Because a blind person is not legally responsible.

Key Takeaway
The hadd of theft requires nine precise conditions; any missing condition, such as the thief's blindness or swallowing the item, averts the cutting of the hand and triggers only civil liability.

One Confession Suffices for Hadd: The Hanafi Position and Refutation of Abu Yusuf
Ruling with proof: basic condition for hadd and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of confessions required for the hadd of cutting, and explain why Abu Yusuf's opinion is rejected.

Core Idea
One confession suffices for the hadd of theft; requiring two would contradict the nature of iqrar.

The passage opens the Book of Theft with a clear ruling: the hadd of cutting is established by a single confession or the testimony of two men. However, there is an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether one confession is enough. This lesson examines the arguments and determines the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
From the matn, the hadd is established by either one confession or two witnesses. Note that the nisab must be reached for each thief if multiple are involved.
2
Locate the ikhtilaf
The commentator flags that 'once' is a refutation of Abu Yusuf, who requires two confessions. Find the exact basis for Abu Yusuf's view.
Abu Yusuf analogizes to testimony in zina.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that confession is not subject to the same suspicion as testimony, and sufficient by itself, similar to qisas and the hadd of qadhf.
The key phrase: 'لا تهمه' (no suspicion against him).
4
Evaluate Abu Yusuf's counterargument
Abu Yusuf analogizes confession to testimony, which in zina requires four witnesses. The Hanafi response shows this analogy fails due to the specific text for zina.
The passage says 'اشتراط الزيادة في الزنا بخلاف القياس'.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The majority view (once) is the relied-upon position. Understand the practical consequence: a thief who confesses once is cut off.

قوله : ( فيقطع أن أقر مرة أو شهد رجلان بيان الحكمها وسبب ثبوتها. وفي قوله «مرة» رد على أبي يوسف في قوله «لا يقطع إلا بإقراره مرتين ويروى عنه أنهما في مجلسين مختلفين لأنه أحد الحجتين فتعتبر بالأخرى وهي البينة كذلك اعتبرنا في الزنا. ولهما أن السرقة ظهرت بإقراره مرة واحدة فيكتفى به كما في القصاص وحد القذف ولا اعتبار بالشهادة فيها لأن الزيادة تفيد فيها تقليل تهمة الكذب ولا تفيد في الإقرار شيئاً لأنه لا تهمه، وباب الرجوع في حق الحد لا ينسد بالتكرار والرجوع في حق المال لا أصلاً لأن صاحب المال يكذبه واشتراط الزيادة في الزنا بخلاف القياس فيقتصر على مورد الشرع. ومن مسائل الإقرار لو قال أنا سارق هذا الثوب بالإضافة قطع، ولو نون القاف لا يقطع لأنه على الاستقبال والأول على الحال. وفي عيون المسائل : قال سرقت من فلان مائة درهم بل عشرة دنانير يقطع في العشرة دنانير ويضمن مائة . هذا إن ادعى المقر له المالين وهو قول أبي حنيفة رجع عن الإقرار رقة مائة وأقر بعشرة دنانير فصح رجوعه عن الإقرار بالسرقة الأولى في حق القطع ولم يصح في حق الضمان وصح الإقرار بالسرقة الثانية في حق القطع، وبه ينتفي الضمان بخلاف ما لو قال سرقت مائة بل مائتين فإنه يقطع ولا يضمن شيئاً لو ادعى المقر له المائتين لأنه أقر بسرقة مائتين ووجب القطع فانتفى الضمان والمائة الأولى لا يدعيها المقر له بخلاف الأولى. ولو قال سرقت مائتين بل مائة لم يقطع ويضمن المائتين لأنه أقر بسرقة عنها فانتفى الضمان ولم يجب القطع ولم يصح الإقرار بالمائة إذ لا يدعيها

المسروق منه، ولو أنه صدقه في الرجوع إلى المائة لا ضمان؛ كذا في فتح القدير. ولم يذكر المصنف صحة الرجوع عن الإقرار للعلم بأنه يصح الرجوع عن الإقرار بالحدود كلها إلا حد القذف . قال في الذخيرة : ة: وإذا أقر بالسرقة ثم هرب لا يتبع وإن كان في فوره اهـ. بخلاف ما إذا شهدا عليه ثم هرب فإنه يتبع ؛ كذا في الظهيرية. ولم يشترط المصنف عدم التقادم في هذه الحجة لأنه ليس بشرط في الإقرار وشرط في البينة فلو أقر بسرقة متقادمة قطع ولو شهدا عليه بذلك لا كما في البدائع وقدمناه وحد التقادم في السرقة هو حده في الزنا؛ كذا في الذخيرة وأطلق في المقر فشمل الحر والعبد وسيأتي تفاصيلها في العبد. وقيد بالرجلين لأن شهادة النساء غير مقبولة فيه وكذا الشهادة على الشهادة وإن قبلت في حق المال. وأفاد بحصر الحجة فيما ذكر أنه لا يقطع بالنكول وإن ضمن المال، وأن العبد لا يقطع بإقرار مولاه عليه بها وإن لزم المال. ولم يقيد المصنف الإقرار بالطواعية . قال في الظهيرية : وإذا أقر بالسرقة مكرهاً فإقراره باطل ومن المتأخرين من أفتى بصحته، وسئل الحسن بن زياد أيحل ضرب السارق حتى يقر ؟ قال : مالم يقطع اللحم لا يتبين العظم ولم يزد على هذا وفي التجنيس : لا يفتى بعقوبة السارق لأنه جور ولا يفتى به .

لا يقر
وفي الظهيرية : هل ينبغي للسارق أن يعلم صاحب المتاع أنه سرق متاعه؟ إن كان لا يخاف أن يظلمه متى أخبره يخبره ليصل إلى حقه، وإن كان يخاف لا يخبره لأنه معذور في ترك الإخبار ولكن يوصل الحق إليه بطريق آخر. وإذا قضى القاضي بالقطع ببينة أو إقرار ثم قال المسروق منه هذا متاعه لم يسرقه مني إنما كنت أودعته أو قال شهد شهودي بزور أو قال أقر هو بباطل أو ما أشبه ذلك سقط عنه القطع، ويستحب للإمام أن يلقن السارق حتى بالسرقة لما . روي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أتى بسارق فقال : أسرق ما إخاله سرق؟ ولأنه احتيال للدرء. وقوله «إخاله» بكسر الهمزة معناه أظنه، وبالفتح كذلك وكلاهما فعل مضارع من المخيلة وهي الظن إلا أن الحديث جاء بالكسر. وإذا شهد كافران على كافر ومسلم بسرقة مال لا يقطع الكافر كما لا يقطع المسلم، ولو شهدا أنه سرق من فلان ثوباً فقال أحدهما إنه هروي وقال الآخر إنه مروي - بسكون الراء ـ ذكر في نسخ أبي سليمان أنه على الخلاف اعتباراً باختلاف الشاهدين في لون البقرة، وذكر في نسخة أبي حفص أنه لا تقبل الشهادة اجماعاً اهـ. ولم يذكر المصنف سؤال الشاهدين. وفي الهداية : وينبغي أن يسألهم الإمام عن كيفية السرقة وماهيتها وزمانها ومكانها لزيادة الاحتياط كما في الحدود، ويحبسه إلى أن يسأل عن
قال : فلا يجب الضمان. قوله : (وحد التقادم في السرقة هو حده في الزنا) قال الرملي : وتقدم أن الفتوى على أنه مقدر بشهر وتقدم أنه إذا كان لعذر تقبل. قوله : (ومن المتأخرين من أفتى بصحته) ظاهر إطلاقه صحته في حق المال والقطع وفيه نظر فإن في ذلك شبهة قوية فكيف يقطع معها،
Book of Theft. If he confesses once or two men testify, even if they are assembled and the taker is one of them, they are cut off (amputated) provided that each of them reaches the nisab threshold. It is not valid... His saying: 'then he is cut off if he confesses once or two men testify' is a statement of its ruling and the cause of its establishment. In his saying 'once' is a refutation of Abu Yusuf who says 'he is not cut off except by his confession twice' and it is narrated from him that they are in two different sessions because it is one of two proofs, so it is evaluated by the other, which is the evidence (al-bayyinah); similarly we considered it in zina. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the theft appeared by his confession once, so it is sufficient, as in qisas and the hadd of qadhf, and testimony is not considered in it because increase in it reduces the suspicion of lying, and it does not increase anything in confession because there is no suspicion against him. The door of retraction in the matter of hadd is not closed by repetition, and retraction in the matter of property is not [closed] at all because the owner of the property denies him. The condition of increase in zina is contrary to analogy so it is restricted to the matter of the law. Among the issues of confession: if he says 'I am the thief of this garment' with idafa, he is cut off; if he puts tanwin on 'qaf', he is not cut off because it is for the future, and the first is for the present. In 'Uyun al-Masa'il: He said 'I stole from Zayd one hundred dirhams but rather ten dinars' - he is cut off for the ten dinars and is liable for one hundred. This is if the person to whom the confession is made claims the two properties, and it is the saying of Abu Hanifa: he retracted from the confession of one hundred and confessed to ten dinars; so his retraction from the confession of the first theft is valid regarding the cutting and not valid regarding the liability, and the confession of the second theft is valid regarding the cutting, and thereby liability is negated. Unlike if he said 'I stole one hundred but rather two hundred' - then he is cut off and does not owe anything if the person to whom the confession is made claims the two hundred, because he confessed to theft of two hundred and cutting becomes obligatory, so liability is negated, and the person to whom the confession is made does not claim the first one hundred, unlike the first case. If he said 'I stole two hundred but rather one hundred', he is not cut off and is liable for two hundred because he confessed to theft of two hundred and retracted from it, so liability is negated? (actually the text is complex) ... and the correctness of his retraction from the confession is known because it is valid to retract from confessions in all hadd penalties except the hadd of qadhf. It is said in al-Dhakhira: when he confesses to theft then flees, he is not pursued even if immediately, unlike if two testified against him then he fled, then he is pursued. The author did not stipulate the absence of time lapse in this proof because it is not a condition in confession but is a condition in testimony; so if he confesses to an old theft, he is cut off; but if two testify about that, no, as in al-Bada'i'. The time limit for theft is the same as that for zina. He generalized the confeser to include free and slave, details will come regarding the slave. He restricted to the two men because the testimony of women is not accepted in it, likewise testimony upon testimony, even if accepted regarding property. It is derived from restricting the proof to what was mentioned that he is not cut off by nukul (refusal to swear) even if he is liable for the property, and that a slave is not cut off by the confession of his master against him even if liability for property is incurred. The author did not restrict confession to being voluntary. In al-Zahira: if he confesses to theft under duress, his confession is void; later scholars gave fatwa of its validity. Hasan b. Ziyad was asked: is it permissible to beat the thief until he confesses? He said: as long as the meat is not cut and the bone is not exposed, and did not add more. In al-Tajnis: fatwa is not given regarding punishment of the thief because it is oppression and fatwa is not given for it. In al-Zahira: should the thief inform the owner that he stole his possession? If he does not fear that he will oppress him when he informs him, he informs him to connect him to his right. If he fears, he does not inform him because he is excused in leaving informing, but he should deliver the right to him by another means. If the judge rules for cutting based on testimony or confession, then the person from whom the property was stolen says 'this is my property, he did not steal it from me, I only deposited it with him' or says 'my witnesses testified falsely' or says 'he confessed falsely' or the like, the cutting is dropped from him. It is recommended for the imam to prompt the thief even [to retract] regarding the theft, because it is narrated that the Prophet was brought a thief and said: 'Did you steal? I do not think he stole.' And because it is a trick to prevent the punishment. If two disbelievers testify against a disbeliever and a Muslim regarding theft of property, the disbeliever is not cut off just as the Muslim is not cut off. If they testify that he stole a garment from Zayd, and one says it is Harawi and the other says it is Marwi (with sukun on ra'), it is mentioned in the copies of Abu Sulayman that it is a matter of disagreement considering the disagreement of the two witnesses regarding the color of the cow; and in the copy of Abu Hafs that the testimony is not accepted by consensus. The author did not mention questioning the two witnesses. In al-Hidaya: the imam should ask them about the how, what, time, and place of the theft for increased caution as in hadd penalties, and he should imprison him until he asks about ...
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expanding on the rulings of theft (sariqa) regarding confession (iqrar) and testimony (shahada). The commentary opens by explaining the matn: 'If he confesses once or two men testify... they are cut off provided the nisab is reached.' The author immediately notes that the word 'once' in the matn refutes Abu Yusuf's position that two confessions are required, with a narration that they must be in two different sittings. The Hanafi argument (of Imam Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) is that theft is proven by a single confession, just as in qisas and the hadd of qadhf. Testimony requires two witnesses to reduce the risk of lying, but confession has no such suspicion. The commentary then discusses detailed issues of confession wording, such as saying 'I am the thief of this garment' (with idafa) vs 'I am a thief' (with tanwin) – the latter indicates future intent so no cutting. The famous case from 'Uyun al-Masa'il is presented: if someone says 'I stole 100 dirhams but rather 10 dinars', the ruling depends on who claims what. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) is that the thief is cut off for the 10 dinars and liable for the 100 dirhams, with the retraction from the first confession valid for cutting but not for liability. The passage also covers retraction from confession: it is valid to retract from all hadd confessions except qadhf. Other topics include: fleeing after confession vs after testimony, time lapse (taqadum), testimony of women, confession under duress, advising the thief to inform the owner, the judge's role in prompting retraction, conflicting testimony about the stolen item, and the procedure for questioning witnesses. The commentary consistently applies Hanafi principles such as 'hudud are averted by doubts' and 'theft requires a nisab'.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Confession or admission of a right or crime. In theft, it is one of the two proofs (along with testimony) that can establish liability for hadd.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given by witnesses in court. For theft, two male witnesses are required; women's testimony is not accepted for hadd but may be accepted for financial liability.
حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Islamic law for specific crimes (theft, zina, qadhf, etc.). It is a right of Allah and cannot be changed by human discretion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum number of confessions required for the hadd of cutting to be applied?
A) One confession
B) Two confessions in one session
C) Two confessions in two different sessions
D) Four confessions

Key Takeaway
One confession suffices for the hadd of cutting; this is the mufta bihi position of the Hanafi school.

The Effect of Wording in a Confession of Theft (Idafa vs Tanwin)
Ruling on the effect of language in confession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a confession that uses idafa (present) and tanwin (future), and state the ruling in each case.

Core Idea
A confession phrased as 'I am the thief of this garment' results in cutting; 'I am a thief' does not, because it indicates future intent.

The commentary continues with linguistic nuances in the wording of confession. The precise phrasing can determine whether the hadd is applied. The key distinction is between a confession that refers to a specific past act (using idafa) and a general future-oriented statement (with tanwin).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two formulations
The passage presents two ways a thief might say 'I am a thief' in Arabic. First: with idafa (اضافة) linking the noun to the stolen object: 'أنا سارق هذا الثوب'. Second: with tanwin (تنوين) on the noun: 'أنا سارق' without specification.
Idafa makes the confession specific to a particular theft.
2
Analyze the difference in meaning
With idafa, the confession refers to the present (الحال) actuality of being the thief of that garment. With tanwin, the word 'سارق' is indefinite and can indicate future tense (الاستقبال) – meaning 'I will be a thief' or 'I am a thief generally'.
The future tense does not confirm a past theft.
3
Derive the ruling
Since the hadd requires a clear admission of a past completed theft, the idafa form confirms this and cutting is applied. The tanwin form leaves doubt about whether the theft actually occurred, so cutting is not applied.
Later commentary notes potential ambiguity in both forms, but the primary ruling stands.

Book of Theft. If he confesses once or two men testify, even if they are assembled and the taker is one of them, they are cut off (amputated) provided that each of them reaches the nisab threshold. It is not valid... His saying: 'then he is cut off if he confesses once or two men testify' is a statement of its ruling and the cause of its establishment. In his saying 'once' is a refutation of Abu Yusuf who says 'he is not cut off except by his confession twice' and it is narrated from him that they are in two different sessions because it is one of two proofs, so it is evaluated by the other, which is the evidence (al-bayyinah); similarly we considered it in zina. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the theft appeared by his confession once, so it is sufficient, as in qisas and the hadd of qadhf, and testimony is not considered in it because increase in it reduces the suspicion of lying, and it does not increase anything in confession because there is no suspicion against him. The door of retraction in the matter of hadd is not closed by repetition, and retraction in the matter of property is not [closed] at all because the owner of the property denies him. The condition of increase in zina is contrary to analogy so it is restricted to the matter of the law. Among the issues of confession: if he says 'I am the thief of this garment' with idafa, he is cut off; if he puts tanwin on 'qaf', he is not cut off because it is for the future, and the first is for the present. In 'Uyun al-Masa'il: He said 'I stole from Zayd one hundred dirhams but rather ten dinars' - he is cut off for the ten dinars and is liable for one hundred. This is if the person to whom the confession is made claims the two properties, and it is the saying of Abu Hanifa: he retracted from the confession of one hundred and confessed to ten dinars; so his retraction from the confession of the first theft is valid regarding the cutting and not valid regarding the liability, and the confession of the second theft is valid regarding the cutting, and thereby liability is negated. Unlike if he said 'I stole one hundred but rather two hundred' - then he is cut off and does not owe anything if the person to whom the confession is made claims the two hundred, because he confessed to theft of two hundred and cutting becomes obligatory, so liability is negated, and the person to whom the confession is made does not claim the first one hundred, unlike the first case. If he said 'I stole two hundred but rather one hundred', he is not cut off and is liable for two hundred because he confessed to theft of two hundred and retracted from it, so liability is negated? (actually the text is complex) ... and the correctness of his retraction from the confession is known because it is valid to retract from confessions in all hadd penalties except the hadd of qadhf. It is said in al-Dhakhira: when he confesses to theft then flees, he is not pursued even if immediately, unlike if two testified against him then he fled, then he is pursued. The author did not stipulate the absence of time lapse in this proof because it is not a condition in confession but is a condition in testimony; so if he confesses to an old theft, he is cut off; but if two testify about that, no, as in al-Bada'i'. The time limit for theft is the same as that for zina. He generalized the confeser to include free and slave, details will come regarding the slave. He restricted to the two men because the testimony of women is not accepted in it, likewise testimony upon testimony, even if accepted regarding property. It is derived from restricting the proof to what was mentioned that he is not cut off by nukul (refusal to swear) even if he is liable for the property, and that a slave is not cut off by the confession of his master against him even if liability for property is incurred. The author did not restrict confession to being voluntary. In al-Zahira: if he confesses to theft under duress, his confession is void; later scholars gave fatwa of its validity. Hasan b. Ziyad was asked: is it permissible to beat the thief until he confesses? He said: as long as the meat is not cut and the bone is not exposed, and did not add more. In al-Tajnis: fatwa is not given regarding punishment of the thief because it is oppression and fatwa is not given for it. In al-Zahira: should the thief inform the owner that he stole his possession? If he does not fear that he will oppress him when he informs him, he informs him to connect him to his right. If he fears, he does not inform him because he is excused in leaving informing, but he should deliver the right to him by another means. If the judge rules for cutting based on testimony or confession, then the person from whom the property was stolen says 'this is my property, he did not steal it from me, I only deposited it with him' or says 'my witnesses testified falsely' or says 'he confessed falsely' or the like, the cutting is dropped from him. It is recommended for the imam to prompt the thief even [to retract] regarding the theft, because it is narrated that the Prophet was brought a thief and said: 'Did you steal? I do not think he stole.' And because it is a trick to prevent the punishment. If two disbelievers testify against a disbeliever and a Muslim regarding theft of property, the disbeliever is not cut off just as the Muslim is not cut off. The author did not mention questioning the two witnesses. Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expanding on the rulings of theft (sariqa) regarding confession (iqrar) and testimony (shahada). The commentary opens by explaining the matn: 'If he confesses once or two men testify... they are cut off provided the nisab is reached.' The author immediately notes that the word 'once' in the matn refutes Abu Yusuf's position that two confessions are required, with a narration that they must be in two different sittings. Testimony requires two witnesses to reduce the risk of lying, but confession has no such suspicion. The commentary then discusses detailed issues of confession wording, such as saying 'I am the thief of this garment' (with idafa) vs 'I am a thief' (with tanwin) – the latter indicates future intent so no cutting. The famous case from 'Uyun al-Masa'il is presented: if someone says 'I stole 100 dirhams but rather 10 dinars', the ruling depends on who claims what. The commentary consistently applies Hanafi principles such as 'hudud are averted by doubts' and 'theft requires a nisab'.

Key Terms
إضافة (idafa): The construct state in Arabic grammar, where a noun is directly linked to the following noun, indicating specificity. In confession, it ties the thief to a specific object.
تنوين (tanwin): The nunation (tanwin) on the end of a noun, making it indefinite. In 'سارق' (thief), tanwin indicates generality and future possibility.

Key Takeaway
A valid confession for hadd must be specific and refer to a past act; indefinite wording like 'I am a thief' (tanwin) is insufficient.

Change and Retraction in Confession: The '100 Dirhams but Rather 10 Dinars' Case
Ruling on retraction and change in confession with multiple items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules on retraction (ruju') when a thief changes his confession, and determine the effect on hadd and financial liability.

Core Idea
When a thief retracts a confession regarding hadd, the punishment drops, but financial liability remains if the owner claims the property.

The passage presents a complex case where a thief first confesses to stealing 100 dirhams, then changes to confessing 10 dinars (with retraction of the first). The Hanafi ruling distinguishes between the effect on the hadd (cutting) and the effect on financial liability. This lesson dissects the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
The thief says: 'I stole from Zayd 100 dirhams, but rather (بل) 10 dinars.' He has made two confessions: first 100 dirhams, then retracted that and confessed 10 dinars.
The word 'بل' indicates a retraction and replacement.
2
Check the owner's claim
The ruling depends on what the owner claims. Here, the owner claims both amounts (100 dirhams and 10 dinars). Abu Hanifa's ruling applies.
If the owner only claims one, the outcome differs.
3
Apply the retraction rule
The retraction of the first theft (100 dirhams) is valid for the hadd (cutting) but not for the financial liability. So cutting is not applied for the first theft, but the thief still owes 100 dirhams because the owner claims it.
Retraction in hadd is valid; in property it is not if owner denies.
4
Evaluate the second confession
The second confession (10 dinars) is a new theft. It is valid for both cutting (if nisab met) and liability. Since the owner claims 10 dinars, liability for that amount is established.
Cutting is applied for the second theft because the confession is not retracted.
5
Determine the overall outcome
The thief is cut off for the 10 dinars (if nisab met) and must pay 100 dirhams (first theft liability) plus 10 dinars? Wait – the passage says 'يقطع في العشرة دنانير ويضمن مائة'. So cutting for 10 dinars, liability for 100 dirhams. The 10 dinars liability is subsumed? Actually, the text says 'وبه ينتفي الضمان' meaning liability for the second theft is negated because cutting and liability do not combine? This needs careful explanation.
The passage later explains that if cutting is applied, the financial liability for that same theft is dropped (لا يجتمع قطع وضمان). So for the 10 dinars, no liability, only cutting.

إن أقر مرة أو شهد رجلان ولو جمعا والآخذ بعضهم قطعوا إن أصاب لكل نصاب ولا
يصح

قوله : ( فيقطع أن أقر مرة أو شهد رجلان بيان الحكمها وسبب ثبوتها. وفي قوله «مرة» رد على أبي يوسف في قوله «لا يقطع إلا بإقراره مرتين ويروى عنه أنهما في مجلسين مختلفين لأنه أحد الحجتين فتعتبر بالأخرى وهي البينة كذلك اعتبرنا في الزنا. ولهما أن السرقة ظهرت بإقراره مرة واحدة فيكتفى به كما في القصاص وحد القذف ولا اعتبار بالشهادة فيها لأن الزيادة تفيد فيها تقليل تهمة الكذب ولا تفيد في الإقرار شيئاً لأنه لا تهمه، وباب الرجوع في حق الحد لا ينسد بالتكرار والرجوع في حق المال لا أصلاً لأن صاحب المال يكذبه واشتراط الزيادة في الزنا بخلاف القياس فيقتصر على مورد الشرع. ومن مسائل الإقرار لو قال أنا سارق هذا الثوب بالإضافة قطع، ولو نون القاف لا يقطع لأنه على الاستقبال والأول على الحال. وفي عيون المسائل : قال سرقت من فلان مائة درهم بل عشرة دنانير يقطع في العشرة دنانير ويضمن مائة . هذا إن ادعى المقر له المالين وهو قول أبي حنيفة رجع عن الإقرار رقة مائة وأقر بعشرة دنانير فصح رجوعه عن الإقرار بالسرقة الأولى في حق القطع ولم يصح في حق الضمان وصح الإقرار بالسرقة الثانية في حق القطع، وبه ينتفي الضمان بخلاف ما لو قال سرقت مائة بل مائتين فإنه يقطع ولا يضمن شيئاً لو ادعى المقر له المائتين لأنه أقر بسرقة مائتين ووجب القطع فانتفى الضمان والمائة الأولى لا يدعيها المقر له بخلاف الأولى. ولو قال سرقت مائتين بل مائة لم يقطع ويضمن المائتين لأنه أقر بسرقة عنها فانتفى الضمان ولم يجب القطع ولم يصح الإقرار بالمائة إذ لا يدعيها
لأنه 
مائتين ورجع 
بسر
وعدمه صحيحة إلا أن كونه يعلم أو لا يعلم وهو المراد في نفس الأمر لا يطلع عليه ولا يثبت إلا بالإقرار، وما تقدم هو ما إذا لم يقر بعلمه بما في الثوب فإنه لا يقطع حتى يكون معه دلالة القصد إليه وذلك بأن يكون كيساً فيه الدراهم فلا يقبل قوله لم أقصد لم أعلم .اهـ. وهو توفيق حسن. قوله : (وباب الرجوع الخ جواب عما قد يقال فائدته رفع احتمال كونه يرجع عنه . قوله: (لأنه على الاستقبال والأول على الحال قال في النهر كذا في الفتح والظاهر أن يقال إن مع التنوين يحتمل الحال والاستقبال فلا يقطع بالشك لكن بقي أن هذا الاحتمال ثابت مع الإضافة أيضاً فكان أن ينبغي لا يقطع أيضاً فتدبره .اهـ. هذا وفي شرح الوهبانية لابن الشحنة قلت : والقطع المذكور بإحرازه وعدم رجوعه، أما لو رجع قبل رجوعه كما تقدم وينبغي أن لا يجري في هذا الإطلاق لأن العوام لا يفرقون فيفرق بين العالم والجاهل اللهم إلا أن يقال يجعل هذا شبهة في درء الحد وفيه بعد والله تعالى أعلم اهـ . قوله : (لأنه أقر بسرقة مائتين ورجع عنها قال الرملي : يعني فوجب ضمانهما بالإقرار ولا يجتمع قطع وضمان ورجوعه عن المائة صح في حق القطع ولم يصح في حق الضمان والمسروق منه المائتين المقر بهما أولاً ولا يدعي المائة التي أضرب عنها بانفرادها فقط تأمل. قوله: (فانتفى الضمان ولم يجب القطع كذا في عامة النسخ وفي نسخة فلا ينتفي وهو الموافق لما في الفتح حيث

المسروق منه، ولو أنه صدقه في الرجوع إلى المائة لا ضمان؛ كذا في فتح القدير. ولم يذكر المصنف صحة الرجوع عن الإقرار للعلم بأنه يصح الرجوع عن الإقرار بالحدود كلها إلا حد القذف . قال في الذخيرة : ة: وإذا أقر بالسرقة ثم هرب لا يتبع وإن كان في فوره اهـ. بخلاف ما إذا شهدا عليه ثم هرب فإنه يتبع ؛ كذا في الظهيرية. ولم يشترط المصنف عدم التقادم في هذه الحجة لأنه ليس بشرط في الإقرار وشرط في البينة فلو أقر بسرقة متقادمة قطع ولو شهدا عليه بذلك لا كما في البدائع وقدمناه وحد التقادم في السرقة هو حده في الزنا؛ كذا في الذخيرة وأطلق في المقر فشمل الحر والعبد وسيأتي تفاصيلها في العبد. وقيد بالرجلين لأن شهادة النساء غير مقبولة فيه وكذا الشهادة على الشهادة وإن قبلت في حق المال. وأفاد بحصر الحجة فيما ذكر أنه لا يقطع بالنكول وإن ضمن المال، وأن العبد لا يقطع بإقرار مولاه عليه بها وإن لزم المال. ولم يقيد المصنف الإقرار بالطواعية . قال في الظهيرية : وإذا أقر بالسرقة مكرهاً فإقراره باطل ومن المتأخرين من أفتى بصحته، وسئل الحسن بن زياد أيحل ضرب السارق حتى يقر ؟ قال : مالم يقطع اللحم لا يتبين العظم ولم يزد على هذا وفي التجنيس : لا يفتى بعقوبة السارق لأنه جور ولا يفتى به .
