"
لا يقر
وفي الظهيرية : هل ينبغي للسارق أن يعلم صاحب المتاع أنه سرق متاعه؟ إن كان لا يخاف أن يظلمه متى أخبره يخبره ليصل إلى حقه، وإن كان يخاف لا يخبره لأنه معذور في ترك الإخبار ولكن يوصل الحق إليه بطريق آخر. وإذا قضى القاضي بالقطع ببينة أو إقرار ثم قال المسروق منه هذا متاعه لم يسرقه مني إنما كنت أودعته أو قال شهد شهودي بزور أو قال أقر هو بباطل أو ما أشبه ذلك سقط عنه القطع، ويستحب للإمام أن يلقن السارق حتى بالسرقة لما . روي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أتى بسارق فقال : أسرق ما إخاله سرق؟ ولأنه احتيال للدرء. وقوله «إخاله» بكسر الهمزة معناه أظنه، وبالفتح كذلك وكلاهما فعل مضارع من المخيلة وهي الظن إلا أن الحديث جاء بالكسر. وإذا شهد كافران على كافر ومسلم بسرقة مال لا يقطع الكافر كما لا يقطع المسلم، ولو شهدا أنه سرق من فلان ثوباً فقال أحدهما إنه هروي وقال الآخر إنه مروي - بسكون الراء ـ ذكر في نسخ أبي سليمان أنه على الخلاف اعتباراً باختلاف الشاهدين في لون البقرة، وذكر في نسخة أبي حفص أنه لا تقبل الشهادة اجماعاً اهـ. ولم يذكر المصنف سؤال الشاهدين. وفي الهداية : وينبغي أن يسألهم الإمام عن كيفية السرقة وماهيتها وزمانها ومكانها لزيادة الاحتياط كما في الحدود، ويحبسه إلى أن يسأل عن
قال : فلا يجب الضمان. قوله : (وحد التقادم في السرقة هو حده في الزنا) قال الرملي : وتقدم أن الفتوى على أنه مقدر بشهر وتقدم أنه إذا كان لعذر تقبل. قوله : (ومن المتأخرين من أفتى بصحته) ظاهر إطلاقه صحته في حق المال والقطع وفيه نظر فإن في ذلك شبهة قوية فكيف يقطع معها،
Book of Theft. If he confesses once or two men testify, even if they are assembled and the taker is one of them, they are cut off (amputated) provided that each of them reaches the nisab threshold. It is not valid... His saying: 'then he is cut off if he confesses once or two men testify' is a statement of its ruling and the cause of its establishment. In his saying 'once' is a refutation of Abu Yusuf who says 'he is not cut off except by his confession twice' and it is narrated from him that they are in two different sessions because it is one of two proofs, so it is evaluated by the other, which is the evidence (al-bayyinah); similarly we considered it in zina. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the theft appeared by his confession once, so it is sufficient, as in qisas and the hadd of qadhf, and testimony is not considered in it because increase in it reduces the suspicion of lying, and it does not increase anything in confession because there is no suspicion against him. The door of retraction in the matter of hadd is not closed by repetition, and retraction in the matter of property is not [closed] at all because the owner of the property denies him. The condition of increase in zina is contrary to analogy so it is restricted to the matter of the law. Among the issues of confession: if he says 'I am the thief of this garment' with idafa, he is cut off; if he puts tanwin on 'qaf', he is not cut off because it is for the future, and the first is for the present. In 'Uyun al-Masa'il: He said 'I stole from Zayd one hundred dirhams but rather ten dinars' - he is cut off for the ten dinars and is liable for one hundred. This is if the person to whom the confession is made claims the two properties, and it is the saying of Abu Hanifa: he retracted from the confession of one hundred and confessed to ten dinars; so his retraction from the confession of the first theft is valid regarding the cutting and not valid regarding the liability, and the confession of the second theft is valid regarding the cutting, and thereby liability is negated. Unlike if he said 'I stole one hundred but rather two hundred' - then he is cut off and does not owe anything if the person to whom the confession is made claims the two hundred, because he confessed to theft of two hundred and cutting becomes obligatory, so liability is negated, and the person to whom the confession is made does not claim the first one hundred, unlike the first case. If he said 'I stole two hundred but rather one hundred', he is not cut off and is liable for two hundred because he confessed to theft of two hundred and retracted from it, so liability is negated? (actually the text is complex) ... and the correctness of his retraction from the confession is known because it is valid to retract from confessions in all hadd penalties except the hadd of qadhf. It is said in al-Dhakhira: when he confesses to theft then flees, he is not pursued even if immediately, unlike if two testified against him then he fled, then he is pursued. The author did not stipulate the absence of time lapse in this proof because it is not a condition in confession but is a condition in testimony; so if he confesses to an old theft, he is cut off; but if two testify about that, no, as in al-Bada'i'. The time limit for theft is the same as that for zina. He generalized the confeser to include free and slave, details will come regarding the slave. He restricted to the two men because the testimony of women is not accepted in it, likewise testimony upon testimony, even if accepted regarding property. It is derived from restricting the proof to what was mentioned that he is not cut off by nukul (refusal to swear) even if he is liable for the property, and that a slave is not cut off by the confession of his master against him even if liability for property is incurred. The author did not restrict confession to being voluntary. In al-Zahira: if he confesses to theft under duress, his confession is void; later scholars gave fatwa of its validity. Hasan b. Ziyad was asked: is it permissible to beat the thief until he confesses? He said: as long as the meat is not cut and the bone is not exposed, and did not add more. In al-Tajnis: fatwa is not given regarding punishment of the thief because it is oppression and fatwa is not given for it. In al-Zahira: should the thief inform the owner that he stole his possession? If he does not fear that he will oppress him when he informs him, he informs him to connect him to his right. If he fears, he does not inform him because he is excused in leaving informing, but he should deliver the right to him by another means. If the judge rules for cutting based on testimony or confession, then the person from whom the property was stolen says 'this is my property, he did not steal it from me, I only deposited it with him' or says 'my witnesses testified falsely' or says 'he confessed falsely' or the like, the cutting is dropped from him. It is recommended for the imam to prompt the thief even [to retract] regarding the theft, because it is narrated that the Prophet was brought a thief and said: 'Did you steal? I do not think he stole.' And because it is a trick to prevent the punishment. If two disbelievers testify against a disbeliever and a Muslim regarding theft of property, the disbeliever is not cut off just as the Muslim is not cut off. If they testify that he stole a garment from Zayd, and one says it is Harawi and the other says it is Marwi (with sukun on ra'), it is mentioned in the copies of Abu Sulayman that it is a matter of disagreement considering the disagreement of the two witnesses regarding the color of the cow; and in the copy of Abu Hafs that the testimony is not accepted by consensus. The author did not mention questioning the two witnesses. In al-Hidaya: the imam should ask them about the how, what, time, and place of the theft for increased caution as in hadd penalties, and he should imprison him until he asks about ...
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expanding on the rulings of theft (sariqa) regarding confession (iqrar) and testimony (shahada). The commentary opens by explaining the matn: 'If he confesses once or two men testify... they are cut off provided the nisab is reached.' The author immediately notes that the word 'once' in the matn refutes Abu Yusuf's position that two confessions are required, with a narration that they must be in two different sittings. The Hanafi argument (of Imam Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) is that theft is proven by a single confession, just as in qisas and the hadd of qadhf. Testimony requires two witnesses to reduce the risk of lying, but confession has no such suspicion. The commentary then discusses detailed issues of confession wording, such as saying 'I am the thief of this garment' (with idafa) vs 'I am a thief' (with tanwin) – the latter indicates future intent so no cutting. The famous case from 'Uyun al-Masa'il is presented: if someone says 'I stole 100 dirhams but rather 10 dinars', the ruling depends on who claims what. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) is that the thief is cut off for the 10 dinars and liable for the 100 dirhams, with the retraction from the first confession valid for cutting but not for liability. The passage also covers retraction from confession: it is valid to retract from all hadd confessions except qadhf. Other topics include: fleeing after confession vs after testimony, time lapse (taqadum), testimony of women, confession under duress, advising the thief to inform the owner, the judge's role in prompting retraction, conflicting testimony about the stolen item, and the procedure for questioning witnesses. The commentary consistently applies Hanafi principles such as 'hudud are averted by doubts' and 'theft requires a nisab'.

Key Terms
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction of confession. Valid for hadd penalties (except qadhf) but not for financial liability if the owner claims the property.
بل (bal): The Arabic word 'but rather' used to retract and replace a statement. In confession, it indicates the first statement is abandoned and a new one is made.
ضمان (daman): Liability or compensation for the value of stolen property. It is separate from the hadd penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where the thief says 'I stole 100 dirhams, but rather 10 dinars', what is the ruling on cutting?
A) He is cut off for the 10 dinars only.
B) He is cut off for the 100 dirhams only.
C) He is cut off for both.
D) He is not cut off at all.

Key Takeaway
Retraction of a confession in theft drops the hadd for that theft but does not extinguish financial liability if the owner claims the property.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

Procedural Rules and the Judge's Role in Averting Hadd
Procedural rules for the judge in theft cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the recommended procedures for the judge to avert the hadd, the effect of duress on confession, and the rules for testimony of disbelievers.

Core Idea
The judge should prompt the thief to retract; coerced confessions are void; hudud are averted by any doubt.

The passage shifts to procedural guidelines for the judge and the principles that safeguard against wrongful punishment. It covers the recommendation to prompt retraction (talqin), the invalidity of coerced confessions, and the treatment of witness testimony, including that of disbelievers.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle of prompting retraction
The passage recommends that the judge prompt the thief to retract his confession, citing the Prophet's practice. This is a manifestation of the principle that hudud are averted by doubts.
The hadith: 'أسرق ما إخاله سرق؟' – the Prophet expressed doubt.
2
Analyze the ruling on coerced confession
Confession under duress is void according to Imam Muhammad. Later some scholars allowed it only if no severe harm. The majority view is that it is not valid and the hadd cannot be applied.
Hasan b. Ziyad said beating is allowed only up to a limit.
3
Examine the rules for testimony
Testimony of two disbelievers is not accepted against a Muslim. Also, if witnesses disagree on details (e.g., color of garment), there is ikhtilaf on acceptance. The judge should also question witnesses thoroughly.
Al-Hidaya recommends asking about how, what, when, where.
4
Apply the principle of shubha in these rules
All these rules aim to avoid applying the hadd in cases of doubt. Even if the thief has been convicted, if the owner later says it was not theft, the hadd is dropped.
The passage gives examples: owner says it was a deposit, or witnesses lied.

المسروق منه، ولو أنه صدقه في الرجوع إلى المائة لا ضمان؛ كذا في فتح القدير. ولم يذكر المصنف صحة الرجوع عن الإقرار للعلم بأنه يصح الرجوع عن الإقرار بالحدود كلها إلا حد القذف . قال في الذخيرة : ة: وإذا أقر بالسرقة ثم هرب لا يتبع وإن كان في فوره اهـ. بخلاف ما إذا شهدا عليه ثم هرب فإنه يتبع ؛ كذا في الظهيرية. ولم يشترط المصنف عدم التقادم في هذه الحجة لأنه ليس بشرط في الإقرار وشرط في البينة فلو أقر بسرقة متقادمة قطع ولو شهدا عليه بذلك لا كما في البدائع وقدمناه وحد التقادم في السرقة هو حده في الزنا؛ كذا في الذخيرة وأطلق في المقر فشمل الحر والعبد وسيأتي تفاصيلها في العبد. وقيد بالرجلين لأن شهادة النساء غير مقبولة فيه وكذا الشهادة على الشهادة وإن قبلت في حق المال. وأفاد بحصر الحجة فيما ذكر أنه لا يقطع بالنكول وإن ضمن المال، وأن العبد لا يقطع بإقرار مولاه عليه بها وإن لزم المال. ولم يقيد المصنف الإقرار بالطواعية . قال في الظهيرية : وإذا أقر بالسرقة مكرهاً فإقراره باطل ومن المتأخرين من أفتى بصحته، وسئل الحسن بن زياد أيحل ضرب السارق حتى يقر ؟ قال : مالم يقطع اللحم لا يتبين العظم ولم يزد على هذا وفي التجنيس : لا يفتى بعقوبة السارق لأنه جور ولا يفتى به .

وفي الظهيرية : هل ينبغي للسارق أن يعلم صاحب المتاع أنه سرق متاعه؟ إن كان لا يخاف أن يظلمه متى أخبره يخبره ليصل إلى حقه، وإن كان يخاف لا يخبره لأنه معذور في ترك الإخبار ولكن يوصل الحق إليه بطريق آخر. وإذا قضى القاضي بالقطع ببينة أو إقرار ثم قال المسروق منه هذا متاعه لم يسرقه مني إنما كنت أودعته أو قال شهد شهودي بزور أو قال أقر هو بباطل أو ما أشبه ذلك سقط عنه القطع، ويستحب للإمام أن يلقن السارق حتى بالسرقة لما . روي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أتى بسارق فقال : أسرق ما إخاله سرق؟ ولأنه احتيال للدرء. وقوله «إخاله» بكسر الهمزة معناه أظنه، وبالفتح كذلك وكلاهما فعل مضارع من المخيلة وهي الظن إلا أن الحديث جاء بالكسر. وإذا شهد كافران على كافر ومسلم بسرقة مال لا يقطع الكافر كما لا يقطع المسلم، ولو شهدا أنه سرق من فلان ثوباً فقال أحدهما إنه هروي وقال الآخر إنه مروي - بسكون الراء ـ ذكر في نسخ أبي سليمان أنه على الخلاف اعتباراً باختلاف الشاهدين في لون البقرة، وذكر في نسخة أبي حفص أنه لا تقبل الشهادة اجماعاً اهـ. ولم يذكر المصنف سؤال الشاهدين. وفي الهداية : وينبغي أن يسألهم الإمام عن كيفية السرقة وماهيتها وزمانها ومكانها لزيادة الاحتياط كما في الحدود، ويحبسه إلى أن يسأل عن
قال : فلا يجب الضمان. قوله : (وحد التقادم في السرقة هو حده في الزنا) قال الرملي : وتقدم أن الفتوى على أنه مقدر بشهر وتقدم أنه إذا كان لعذر تقبل. قوله : (ومن المتأخرين من أفتى بصحته) ظاهر إطلاقه صحته في حق المال والقطع وفيه نظر فإن في ذلك شبهة قوية فكيف يقطع معها،
Book of Theft. If he confesses once or two men testify, even if they are assembled and the taker is one of them, they are cut off (amputated) provided that each of them reaches the nisab threshold. It is not valid... His saying: 'then he is cut off if he confesses once or two men testify' is a statement of its ruling and the cause of its establishment. In his saying 'once' is a refutation of Abu Yusuf who says 'he is not cut off except by his confession twice' and it is narrated from him that they are in two different sessions because it is one of two proofs, so it is evaluated by the other, which is the evidence (al-bayyinah); similarly we considered it in zina. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the theft appeared by his confession once, so it is sufficient, as in qisas and the hadd of qadhf, and testimony is not considered in it because increase in it reduces the suspicion of lying, and it does not increase anything in confession because there is no suspicion against him. The door of retraction in the matter of hadd is not closed by repetition, and retraction in the matter of property is not [closed] at all because the owner of the property denies him. The condition of increase in zina is contrary to analogy so it is restricted to the matter of the law. Among the issues of confession: if he says 'I am the thief of this garment' with idafa, he is cut off; if he puts tanwin on 'qaf', he is not cut off because it is for the future, and the first is for the present. In 'Uyun al-Masa'il: He said 'I stole from Zayd one hundred dirhams but rather ten dinars' - he is cut off for the ten dinars and is liable for one hundred. This is if the person to whom the confession is made claims the two properties, and it is the saying of Abu Hanifa: he retracted from the confession of one hundred and confessed to ten dinars; so his retraction from the confession of the first theft is valid regarding the cutting and not valid regarding the liability, and the confession of the second theft is valid regarding the cutting, and thereby liability is negated. Unlike if he said 'I stole one hundred but rather two hundred' - then he is cut off and does not owe anything if the person to whom the confession is made claims the two hundred, because he confessed to theft of two hundred and cutting becomes obligatory, so liability is negated, and the person to whom the confession is made does not claim the first one hundred, unlike the first case. If he said 'I stole two hundred but rather one hundred', he is not cut off and is liable for two hundred because he confessed to theft of two hundred and retracted from it, so liability is negated? (actually the text is complex) ... and the correctness of his retraction from the confession is known because it is valid to retract from confessions in all hadd penalties except the hadd of qadhf. It is said in al-Dhakhira: when he confesses to theft then flees, he is not pursued even if immediately, unlike if two testified against him then he fled, then he is pursued. The author did not stipulate the absence of time lapse in this proof because it is not a condition in confession but is a condition in testimony; so if he confesses to an old theft, he is cut off; but if two testify about that, no, as in al-Bada'i'. The time limit for theft is the same as that for zina. He generalized the confeser to include free and slave, details will come regarding the slave. He restricted to the two men because the testimony of women is not accepted in it, likewise testimony upon testimony, even if accepted regarding property. It is derived from restricting the proof to what was mentioned that he is not cut off by nukul (refusal to swear) even if he is liable for the property, and that a slave is not cut off by the confession of his master against him even if liability for property is incurred. The author did not restrict confession to being voluntary. In al-Zahira: if he confesses to theft under duress, his confession is void; later scholars gave fatwa of its validity. Hasan b. Ziyad was asked: is it permissible to beat the thief until he confesses? He said: as long as the meat is not cut and the bone is not exposed, and did not add more. In al-Tajnis: fatwa is not given regarding punishment of the thief because it is oppression and fatwa is not given for it. In al-Zahira: should the thief inform the owner that he stole his possession? If he does not fear that he will oppress him when he informs him, he informs him to connect him to his right. If he fears, he does not inform him because he is excused in leaving informing, but he should deliver the right to him by another means. If the judge rules for cutting based on testimony or confession, then the person from whom the property was stolen says 'this is my property, he did not steal it from me, I only deposited it with him' or says 'my witnesses testified falsely' or says 'he confessed falsely' or the like, the cutting is dropped from him. It is recommended for the imam to prompt the thief even [to retract] regarding the theft, because it is narrated that the Prophet was brought a thief and said: 'Did you steal? I do not think he stole.' And because it is a trick to prevent the punishment. If two disbelievers testify against a disbeliever and a Muslim regarding theft of property, the disbeliever is not cut off just as the Muslim is not cut off. If they testify that he stole a garment from Zayd, and one says it is Harawi and the other says it is Marwi (with sukun on ra'), it is mentioned in the copies of Abu Sulayman that it is a matter of disagreement considering the disagreement of the two witnesses regarding the color of the cow; and in the copy of Abu Hafs that the testimony is not accepted by consensus. The author did not mention questioning the two witnesses. In al-Hidaya: the imam should ask them about the how, what, time, and place of the theft for increased caution as in hadd penalties, and he should imprison him until he asks about ...
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expanding on the rulings of theft (sariqa) regarding confession (iqrar) and testimony (shahada). The commentary opens by explaining the matn: 'If he confesses once or two men testify... they are cut off provided the nisab is reached.' The author immediately notes that the word 'once' in the matn refutes Abu Yusuf's position that two confessions are required, with a narration that they must be in two different sittings. The Hanafi argument (of Imam Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) is that theft is proven by a single confession, just as in qisas and the hadd of qadhf. Testimony requires two witnesses to reduce the risk of lying, but confession has no such suspicion. The commentary then discusses detailed issues of confession wording, such as saying 'I am the thief of this garment' (with idafa) vs 'I am a thief' (with tanwin) – the latter indicates future intent so no cutting. The famous case from 'Uyun al-Masa'il is presented: if someone says 'I stole 100 dirhams but rather 10 dinars', the ruling depends on who claims what. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) is that the thief is cut off for the 10 dinars and liable for the 100 dirhams, with the retraction from the first confession valid for cutting but not for liability. The passage also covers retraction from confession: it is valid to retract from all hadd confessions except qadhf. Other topics include: fleeing after confession vs after testimony, time lapse (taqadum), testimony of women, confession under duress, advising the thief to inform the owner, the judge's role in prompting retraction, conflicting testimony about the stolen item, and the procedure for questioning witnesses. The commentary consistently applies Hanafi principles such as 'hudud are averted by doubts' and 'theft requires a nisab'.

Key Terms
تلقيــن (talqin): Prompting or coaching the accused to say something, here to retract the confession. It is recommended to avert the hadd.
إكراه (ikrah): Coercion or duress. Confession under ikrah is void according to the Hanafi school.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony. Rules: two male witnesses, no disbelievers against Muslims, consistency required.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the recommended action for a judge upon hearing a confession of theft?
A) Immediately apply the hadd.
B) Prompt the thief to retract.
C) Ask for a witness.
D) Imprison the thief.

Key Takeaway
The judge should actively encourage retraction, reject coerced confessions, and interrogate witnesses to ensure that hudud are applied only on clear proof, reflecting the principle of shubha.

Confession as Proof in Theft: Conditions and Limitations
Explaining conditions for validity of confession in theft

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a confession in theft leads to the hadd penalty and distinguish confession from witness testimony regarding retraction, prescription, and coercion.

Core Idea
Confession in theft is valid even after long delay, but must be voluntary; retraction is allowed except in qadhf.

The proof of theft can be established by confession or by two male witnesses. However, the Hanafi school applies distinct rules to each. In this lesson, we explore the conditions and limitations of confession as a proof, including the validity of retraction, the irrelevance of prescription, the invalidity of coerced confessions, and how this contrasts with witness testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of proof
The passage mentions two proofs: confession (iqrar) and testimony (bayyinah). Note that the author restricts the types of proof that lead to cutting.
Other proofs like nukul do not lead to cutting.
2
Understand retraction of confession
The text states that retraction of confession is valid in all hudud except qadhf. This means a thief can retract and avoid cutting.
This is a unique Hanafi rule.
3
Analyze the role of prescription (taqadum)
Prescription is not a condition for confession, so a confession for an old theft leads to cutting. But for witnesses, prescription is a bar.
The limit of prescription is the same as in zina.
4
Identify the condition of voluntariness
The passage notes that coerced confession is void according to the reliable opinion. This is a key condition.
Some later Hanafis differed, but the mufta bihi is void.
5
Distinguish other limitations
Women's testimony is not accepted in theft, testimony upon testimony is not accepted, and nukul (refusal to swear) does not lead to cutting.
These are limitations on proof, not just confession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السرقة
المسروق منه، ولو أنه صدقه في الرجوع إلى المائة لا ضمان؛ كذا في فتح القدير. ولم يذكر المصنف صحة الرجوع عن الإقرار للعلم بأنه يصح الرجوع عن الإقرار بالحدود كلها إلا حد القذف . قال في الذخيرة : ة: وإذا أقر بالسرقة ثم هرب لا يتبع وإن كان في فوره اهـ. بخلاف ما إذا شهدا عليه ثم هرب فإنه يتبع ؛ كذا في الظهيرية. ولم يشترط المصنف عدم التقادم في هذه الحجة لأنه ليس بشرط في الإقرار وشرط في البينة فلو أقر بسرقة متقادمة قطع ولو شهدا عليه بذلك لا كما في البدائع وقدمناه وحد التقادم في السرقة هو حده في الزنا؛ كذا في الذخيرة وأطلق في المقر فشمل الحر والعبد وسيأتي تفاصيلها في العبد. وقيد بالرجلين لأن شهادة النساء غير مقبولة فيه وكذا الشهادة على الشهادة وإن قبلت في حق المال. وأفاد بحصر الحجة فيما ذكر أنه لا يقطع بالنكول وإن ضمن المال، وأن العبد لا يقطع بإقرار مولاه عليه بها وإن لزم المال. ولم يقيد المصنف الإقرار بالطواعية . قال في الظهيرية : وإذا أقر بالسرقة مكرهاً فإقراره باطل ومن المتأخرين من أفتى بصحته، وسئل الحسن بن زياد أيحل ضرب السارق حتى يقر ؟ قال : مالم يقطع اللحم لا يتبين العظم ولم يزد على هذا وفي التجنيس : لا يفتى بعقوبة السارق لأنه جور ولا يفتى به . المصنف اهـ .
The chapter of theft. From whom the stolen property is taken; if he confirms him in returning the hundred, there is no liability; as in Fath al-Qadir. The author did not mention the validity of retracting the confession because it is known that retracting confession in all hudud is valid except for the hadd of qadhf. It is said in al-Dhakhira: If one confesses to theft then flees, he is not followed even if immediately; unlike if two witnesses testified against him then he fled, then he is followed; as in al-Zahiriyya. The author did not condition lack of prescription in this proof because it is not a condition for confession but is a condition for evidence; so if one confesses to a prescribed theft, he is cut; if two witnesses testify to that, not cut; as in al-Bada'i' and we have presented it. The limit of prescription in theft is its limit in zina; as in al-Dhakhira. He generalizes in the confessor so it includes free and slave; details on the slave will come. He restricted to men because women's testimony is not accepted in it, likewise testimony upon testimony even if accepted in property matters. The restriction of proof to what was mentioned indicates that cutting does not occur by refusal to swear even if liable for property, and that a slave is not cut by his master's confession upon him even if property is due. The author did not restrict confession to willingness. It is said in al-Zahiriyya: If one confesses to theft under coercion, his confession is void; some later scholars gave a fatwa on its validity. Hasan ibn Ziyad was asked: Is it permissible to beat the thief until he confesses? He said: As long as the flesh is not cut and the bone is not exposed, and he did not go beyond this. In al-Tajnis: No fatwa is given for punishing the thief because it is injustice and no fatwa is given. The author ends.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings about the proof of theft through confession. The author, commenting on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explains several conditions and details. First, if the victim confirms that the thief returned the stolen item, there is no liability. The author notes that retracting a confession is valid in all hudud except qadhf. A confessor who flees is not pursued immediately, unlike a witness who flees. Prescription (taqadum) is not a condition for confession, so an old theft confession leads to cutting; but for witnesses, prescription is a condition, so they are not cut. The definition of prescription in theft is the same as in zina. The confessor includes both free and slave. Testimony is limited to men; women's testimony is not accepted, nor is testimony upon testimony for theft. Cutting does not occur by nukul (refusal to swear) even if property is due. A master's confession for his slave does not lead to cutting. Coerced confession is void, though later scholars differed. Beating the thief to get a confession is not allowed beyond light beating. The author concludes that no fatwa is given for punishing the thief unjustly.

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrar): A voluntary acknowledgment of guilt; in theft, it leads to hadd if conditions met.
البينة (al-bayyinah): Proof by two male witnesses; in theft, testimony is subject to conditions like prescription.
التقادم (al-taqadum): The passage of time; in theft, it is defined as the same limit as in zina, and it bars witness testimony but not confession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on retracting a confession of theft?
A) Retraction is not valid under any circumstances.
B) Retraction is valid, just like all hudud except qadhf.
C) Retraction is valid only if the thief flees.
D) Retraction is valid only if made before the judge.

Key Takeaway
Confession in theft is a strong proof that is not barred by prescription, but it must be voluntary and can be retracted except in qadhf, distinguishing it from witness testimony.

Should the Thief Inform the Victim?
Advising the thief and imam on hudud cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a thief should inform the victim, explain the imam's recommendation to prompt denial, and apply the principle of averting hudud with doubts.

Core Idea
Averting hudud with doubts takes precedence even over a thief's confession.

This passage from al-Zahiriyya addresses the thief's ethical duty to inform the victim and the imam's role in averting the hadd punishment. The Hanafi school emphasises avoiding harsh punishments through legal stratagems and doubts, as demonstrated by the Prophet's example.

Guided Path
1
Identify the thief's duty regarding informing
Determine whether the thief should inform the victim based on fear of oppression.
If no fear, he should inform; if fear, he may return the right by other means.
2
Understand the effect of victim's denial after conviction
If the victim denies the theft or declares the evidence false, the hadd is dropped.
This shows that the hadd is not applied if a doubt is raised.
3
Analyze the recommendation for the imam to prompt denial
The imam is encouraged to prompt the thief to deny, following the Prophet's sunnah.
This is a stratagem to avert the hadd, not a command to lie.
4
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet's statement 'Did you steal? I do not think you stole' provides the basis.
The hadith uses indirect phrasing to give the thief an opportunity to retract.
5
Note additional rules on testimony discrepancies
Disagreement in describing the stolen object (e.g., Harawi vs Marwi) leads to rejection of testimony and prevents cutting.
This is consistent with the principle of avoiding hudud through doubts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الظهيرية : هل ينبغي للسارق أن يعلم صاحب المتاع أنه سرق متاعه؟ إن كان لا يخاف أن يظلمه متى أخبره يخبره ليصل إلى حقه، وإن كان يخاف لا يخبره لأنه معذور في ترك الإخبار ولكن يوصل الحق إليه بطريق آخر. وإذا قضى القاضي بالقطع ببينة أو إقرار ثم قال المسروق منه هذا متاعه لم يسرقه مني إنما كنت أودعته أو قال شهد شهودي بزور أو قال أقر هو بباطل أو ما أشبه ذلك سقط عنه القطع، ويستحب للإمام أن يلقن السارق حتى بالسرقة لما . روي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أتى بسارق فقال : أسرق ما إخاله سرق؟ ولأنه احتيال للدرء. وقوله «إخاله» بكسر الهمزة معناه أظنه، وبالفتح كذلك وكلاهما فعل مضارع من المخيلة وهي الظن إلا أن الحديث جاء بالكسر. وإذا شهد كافران على كافر ومسلم بسرقة مال لا يقطع الكافر كما لا يقطع المسلم، ولو شهدا أنه سرق من فلان ثوباً فقال أحدهما إنه هروي وقال الآخر إنه مروي - بسكون الراء ـ ذكر في نسخ أبي سليمان أنه على الخلاف اعتباراً باختلاف الشاهدين في لون البقرة، وذكر في نسخة أبي حفص أنه لا تقبل الشهادة اجماعاً اهـ.
In al-Zahiriyya: Should the thief inform the owner of the goods that he stole his goods? If he does not fear that he will oppress him when he informs him, he should inform him so that he may obtain his right; if he fears, he should not inform him because he is excused in leaving the report, but he should deliver the right by another means. If the judge decides on cutting by evidence or confession, then the victim says: 'This is my goods, he did not steal them from me, rather I had deposited them with him' or says 'My witnesses testified falsely' or says 'He confessed falsely' or something similar, the cutting is dropped. It is recommended for the imam to prompt the thief even regarding the theft, because it is narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, was brought a thief and said: 'Did you steal? I do not think you stole.' And because it is a stratagem for averting [the hadd]. His word 'I do not think' with kasra of the hamza means I think, and with fatha similarly, both are present tense verbs from 'makhila' which is opinion, except that the hadith came with kasra. If two infidels testify against an infidel and a Muslim for theft of property, the infidel is not cut just as the Muslim is not cut. If they testify that he stole a garment from so-and-so, one says it is Harawi and the other says it is Marwi (with sukun of ra), it is mentioned in the copies of Abu Sulayman that it is subject to disagreement considering the difference of witnesses in the color of the cow, and mentioned in the copy of Abu Hafs that the testimony is not accepted by consensus.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage provides guidance on the thief's ethical duty to inform the victim. If no harm is feared, he should inform to return the right; otherwise, he may remain silent and return it by another means. If after a conviction the victim denies the theft, the hadd is dropped. The imam is recommended to prompt the thief even to deny the theft, as the Prophet did, to find a way to avert the hadd, following the principle of 'avert hudud by doubts.' The passage also discusses disagreements on testimony from infidels and discrepancies in describing the stolen item, indicating that such differences can prevent cutting.

Key Terms
التلقين (al-talqin): The imam prompting the thief to deny to avert the hadd.
الظهيرية (al-Zahiriyya): A Hanafi legal work referenced in this passage.
الدرء (al-dar'): Averting or repelling (the hadd).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the recommended action for the imam regarding a thief who has confessed?
A) To immediately order the cutting.
B) To prompt the thief to deny to avert the hadd.
C) To ask the victim to confirm the theft.
D) To ignore the confession.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the hadd punishment for theft is averted by any credible doubt, including the victim's denial, the imam's prompting, or inconsistent testimony.

Defining Prescription (Taqadum) in Theft
Defining the time limit for prescription in theft

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of taqadum in theft and identify when witness testimony is barred by prescription.

Core Idea
Prescription in theft bars witness testimony after one month, but excuses may allow acceptance.

In Islamic criminal law, certain Hudud offenses have a time limit after which witness testimony is no longer accepted. This lesson clarifies that limit for theft (sariqa) as per the Hanafi school, and the important exception for valid excuses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal term
What is the term being defined in this passage? Note that 'taqadum' refers to the time limit for accepting witness testimony.
2
State the ruling
The matn says the limit for theft is the same as for zina. The commentator al-Ramli specifies it is one month per the operative fatwa.
The baseline is one month.
3
Note the exception
If there is a valid excuse (e.g., the victim was absent), the testimony may be accepted even after the period.
Excuses preserve the right to testify.
4
Distinguish testimony from confession
Prescription applies only to witness testimony, not to confession by the accused. If the accused confesses after the period, the Hadd can still be applied.
This is a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وحد التقادم في السرقة هو حده في الزنا) قال الرملي : وتقدم أن الفتوى على أنه مقدر بشهر وتقدم أنه إذا كان لعذر تقبل.
His saying: (And the limit of prescription in theft is its limit in zina) al-Ramli said: And it was previously stated that the fatwa is that it is estimated at a month, and it was previously stated that if there is an excuse, it is accepted.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'taqadum' (prescription) in the context of theft. The matn states that the time limit for prescription in theft is the same as in zina. The commentator al-Ramli clarifies that the operative fatwa is that it is set at one month. However, if there is a valid excuse (such as the victim being absent), the testimony may still be accepted even after that period. This is important because prescription bars witness testimony but not confession.

Key Terms
التقادم (al-taqadum): The time limit after which witness testimony is not accepted; in theft, it is one month.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how long is the period of prescription in theft?
A) One year.
B) One month.
C) Six months.
D) No time limit.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi prescription for theft is one month, but testimony is accepted if there is a valid excuse; prescription does not bar confession.

Coerced Confession in Theft: The Role of Doubt (Shubhah)
Critical refinement of a matn statement on coerced confession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that a coerced confession does not lead to cutting and evaluate the opposing opinion among later Hanafi scholars.

Core Idea
Coercion creates a strong doubt (shubhah), and hudud are averted by doubts—so cutting cannot follow.

This passage addresses a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of coercion on a confession in theft. While some later scholars considered the confession valid for both property and punishment, the commentator firmly rejects that view, invoking the core Hanafi principle that hudud are suspended by the slightest doubt. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of how shubhah operates in hudud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Positions
Identify the ruling claimed by some later Hanafi scholars (that coerced confession is valid and leads to cutting) and the commentator's rejection.
The commentator uses 'fīhi nazar' to indicate criticism.
2
Isolate the Hanafi Principle
Recognize that the commentator's basis is the principle that hudud are averted by shubhah (doubt). Coercion creates a 'shubhah qawiyyah' (strong doubt).
This principle is well-established: 'idra'u al-hududa bi al-shubuhāt'.
3
Apply the Principle to the Case
Determine that since a strong doubt exists, the hadd of cutting must be dropped. The commentator asks rhetorically: 'how can cutting occur with it?'
The doubt affects the confession's reliability, not the act of theft itself.
4
Determine the Practical Consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: If the confession is accepted, the person is cut; if rejected, not cut. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it is void.
Property consequences may be different—some scholars distinguish between property and punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن المتأخرين من أفتى بصحته) ظاهر إطلاقه صحته في حق المال والقطع وفيه نظر فإن في ذلك شبهة قوية فكيف يقطع معها،
His saying: (And some later scholars gave a fatwa on its validity) the apparent meaning of his absolute statement is its validity in property and cutting, but it is debatable because there is a strong doubt in that, so how can cutting occur with it?
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of a matn statement about coerced confession. Some later Hanafi scholars upheld the validity of a coerced confession for both theft and property, but the commentator rejects this, arguing that coercion creates a strong doubt (shubha), and hudud are averted by doubts. Therefore, the cutting should not be carried out. This reflects the Hanafi principle that hudud are suspended in case of any doubt.

Key Terms
الشبهة (al-shubhah): A doubt that prevents application of the hadd punishment; here, coercion creates a strong shubhah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator reject the fatwa that a coerced confession leads to cutting?
A) Because the confession was not made in court.
B) Because coercion creates a strong doubt (shubhah).
C) Because the victim did not complain.
D) Because the thief later retracted.

Key Takeaway
Coerced confession in theft is invalid for hadd because coercion creates a strong doubt, and hudud are averted by doubts.

Questioning Witnesses and the Confessor in Theft Cases
Explaining how the imam should question witnesses and confessor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five elements the imam must inquire about from witnesses in a theft case and explain why the confessor is not asked about time.

Core Idea
Theft amputation requires strict procedural caution – the imam must verify time, place, manner, nature, and property.

This lesson explains the recommended procedure for the imam when hearing testimony or confession in a theft case. Hudud punishments demand extra caution; therefore, the imam is to ask detailed questions to ensure all legal conditions for cutting are met. We will examine each element and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five areas of inquiry for witnesses
From al-Hidayah and al-Kafi, the imam should ask about the manner (how the theft occurred), nature (what was stolen, to distinguish from non-property takings), time (to check prescription), place (to check if in dar al-harb), and the stolen property itself (since not all property theft entails cutting).
The manner excludes cases like piercing a wall and extracting goods without actual taking.
2
Explain the rationale for each question
Each question serves to confirm that the theft meets the strict legal definition for hadd. For example, asking about nature separates property theft from figurative thefts (e.g., eavesdropping), and time ensures the statute of limitations has not passed.
The rationale is rooted in the principle of extra caution in hudud.
3
Note the additional question about the stolen property from al-Kafi
Al-Kafi adds the question about the stolen property because the value and type of property affect whether cutting is obligatory.
This supplements the list from al-Hidayah.
4
Recognize the disagreement on asking about the victim
Imam Muhammad did not require asking about the victim as he is present to litigate, but later scholars like the author of al-Tabyin required it because the victim might be a relative or husband, which could affect the hadd.
The mufta bihi is to ask about the victim.
5
Apply the same to the confessor, noting the exception of time
The confessor is asked about all the same elements except time, because prescription does not apply to confession — once a person confesses, the case is not dismissed due to passage of time.
This nuance prevents the confessor from using delay as a defense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يذكر المصنف سؤال الشاهدين. وفي الهداية : وينبغي أن يسألهم الإمام عن كيفية السرقة وماهيتها وزمانها ومكانها لزيادة الاحتياط كما في الحدود، ويحبسه إلى أن يسأل عن الشهود للتهمة اهـ زاد في الكافي أنه يسألهما عن المسروق إذ سرقة كل مال لا توجب القطع فالسؤال عن الكيفية لاحتمال أنه سرق على كيفية لا يقطع معها كأن نقب الجدار وأدخل يده فأخرج المتاع فإنه لا يقطع والسؤال عن الماهية لإطلاقها على استراق السمع والنقص من أركان الصلاة والسؤال عن الزمان لاحتمال التقادم، وعلى المكان لاحتمال السرقة في دار الحرب من مسلم. وفي المبسوط : لم يذكر محمد السؤال عن المسروق منه لأنه حاضر يخاصم والشهود يشهدون على السرقة منه فلا حاجة إلى السؤال عنه وفيه نظر لاحتمال أن يكون قريب السارق أو زوجاً فلا بد من السؤال عنه كما في التبيين. وأما سؤال المقر فإنه عن جميع ما ذكرنا إلا عن السؤال عن الزمان.
The author did not mention questioning the two witnesses. In al-Hidayah: It is appropriate for the imam to ask them about the manner (how) of the theft, its nature (what), its time, and its place for extra caution as in hudud, and he should imprison them until he asks about the witnesses due to accusation. In al-Kafi it adds that he asks them about the stolen property because not every property theft necessitates cutting. So asking about the manner due to the possibility that he stole in a manner that does not entail cutting, like if he pierced the wall and inserted his hand and took out the goods, then he is not cut. Asking about the nature because the word 'theft' applies to eavesdropping and shortening the pillars of prayer. Asking about time due to possibility of prescription. Asking about place due to possibility of theft in dar al-harb from a Muslim. In al-Mabsut: Muhammad did not mention asking about the victim because he is present litigating and the witnesses testify against him, so no need to ask about him; but there is consideration because he might be a relative of the thief or a husband, so he must be asked as in al-Tabyin. As for questioning the confessor, it is about all we mentioned except the question about time.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage details the procedure for questioning witnesses and the confessor in theft cases. The imam should ask about the manner, nature, time, place, and the stolen property to ensure all conditions for cutting are met. For example, if the theft was through 'piercing' (naqb) without direct taking, there may be no cutting. The nature of 'theft' is linguistically general, so the imam must clarify that it was theft of property, not eavesdropping. Time is asked to check for prescription, place to check if it occurred in dar al-harb. Imam Muhammad did not require asking about the victim, but later scholars required it due to possible relationships. The confessor is asked about everything except time, because prescription does not apply to confession.

Key Terms
الكيفية (al-kayfiyyah): The manner of theft; e.g., whether it was by piercing and extraction which does not entail cutting.
الماهية (al-mahiyyah): The nature/essence of the act; to narrow the general term 'theft' to the legal definition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the imam instructed to ask witnesses about the time of the theft?
A) To determine the season of the year.
B) To check for prescription (taqadum).
C) To verify if the thief had an alibi.
D) To see if the theft occurred during daytime.

Key Takeaway
The imam must exercise caution in theft cases by probing manner, nature, time, place, and property; a confession exempts time due to prescription irrelevance.

Multiple Thieves and the Nisab Requirement
Ruling on group theft and nisab per thief

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when amputation applies to multiple thieves and identify the conditions that must be satisfied for each thief individually.

Core Idea
For cutting to apply to multiple thieves, each must have stolen a nisab individually—group total does not suffice.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a key nuance in the law of theft: when a group steals together, the hadd punishment is not collective. Instead, each thief's liability is assessed independently. The author explains the principle that the cause of cutting is stealing the nisab, and this must be established for each thief. We will break down the conditions, exceptions, and how cooperation is defined.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the phrase 'cut each if for each there is a nisab'. The ruling is that amputation (qat') is wajib for each thief only if that thief individually took a nisab (minimum 10 dirhams) from the stolen property.
The total value taken by the group does not matter; each must reach the nisab threshold.
2
Understand the causal link
The text states 'the cause is stealing the nisab'. The obligation (wujub) of cutting is triggered by the act of taking the nisab. Each thief's act is considered separately, so the nisab must be complete in his share.
This prevents cutting for someone who only assisted or took a negligible amount.
3
Analyze the conditions related to the thieves
List the persons excluded from cutting: any mahram relative of the victim, a child (sabi), an insane person (majnun), or an idiot (ma'tuh). These exempt individuals are not subject to hadd even if they took a nisab.
Mahram refers to individuals permanently prohibited from marrying the victim (e.g., father, son, brother).
4
Examine the requirement of cooperation
The passage explains that cooperation ('al-ta'awun') is achieved if the thieves act together: either all leave the hizr (secure place) together, or one follows immediately after others. This joint action is necessary for the ruling to apply to all.
If they act independently and separately, the group ruling does not apply; each is judged alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو جمعا والآخذ بعضهم قطعوا إن أصاب لكل نصاب) أي لو كان السارق جماعة لأن الموجب سرقة النصاب، ويجب على كل واحد منهم بجنايته فيعتبر كمال النصاب في حقه، وقدمنا أنه لا فرق بين كون الأخذ مباشرة أو تسبباً ولا بد من أن لا يكون فيهم ذو رحم محرم من المسروق منه ولا صبي ولا مجنون ولا معتوه وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا كانوا خرجوا معه من الحرز أو بعده من فوره أو خرج هو بعدهم في فورهم لأن بذلك يحصل التعاون. وقيد بالجمع لأنه لو سرق واحد من عشرة من كل واحد منهم درهماً من بيت واحد والظاهر أنه خاص في حق تضمينه المال فقط لما أنه لا يقطع بالنكول وأنه لو أقر ثم هرب لا يتبع.
His saying: (And if they collected and some of them took, they are cut if for each there is a nisab) meaning if the thieves are a group, because the cause is stealing the nisab, and it is obligatory upon each one according to his offense, so completion of the nisab is considered in his right. And we have stated that there is no difference between taking directly or by causation, and it is necessary that there not be among them a mahram relative of the victim, nor a child, nor an insane person, nor an idiot. He expressed it absolutely so it includes whether they went out with him from the hizr or after him immediately, or he went out after them in their immediate time because cooperation is achieved. He restricted to plurality because if one stole from ten persons a dirham from each from one house, apparently it is specific regarding his liability for property only, because he is not cut by refusal to swear, and if he confesses and then flees, he is not followed.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage comments on the matn regarding multiple thieves. For cutting to apply, each thief must have taken a nisab (minimum value) individually. The offense is per person, so if the total taken is a nisab but each took less, no cutting. Direct taking or causing the taking are equal. Those who are mahram (such as spouse, father) of the victim, children, insane, or idiots are excluded from cutting. Cooperation is defined by immediate joint action or prior planning. The restriction to 'collecting' (jami'an) implies that if one person steals from multiple owners from one house, he is only liable for property, not cutting, and he is not cut if he refuses to swear or confesses and flees.

Key Terms
النصاب (al-nisab): The minimum value (10 dirhams or equivalent) that must be stolen for cutting to be obligatory.
الحرز (al-hizr): A secure place where property is normally kept, such as a locked house or shop.
التعاون (al-ta'awun): Cooperation in theft, established when thieves act together in immediate succession from the hizr.
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahm muharram): A person so closely related to the victim that marriage is permanently prohibited (e.g., father, son, brother).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, which of the following persons is NOT exempt from cutting in a group theft?
A) A person who is the victim's adult brother.
B) A person who is a child under puberty.
C) A person who is insane.
D) A person who is a non-mahram adult of sound mind.

Key Takeaway
For amputation to apply to multiple thieves, each must individually take a nisab; exemptions include mahram relatives, children, and the insane, and cooperation requires immediate joint action.

Questioning the Confessor About Place
Dispute on whether the confessor should be asked about the location

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct Hanafi ruling on whether the confessor in a theft case should be asked about the location and explain the rationale.

Core Idea
The confessor must be asked about the place — a textual corruption suggested otherwise.

This lesson addresses a textual discrepancy in the classical Hanafi text. Some copies of Fath al-Qadir state that the confessor is not asked about the place of theft, but the commentator in al-Nahr identifies this as a corruption. The correct position, according to the relied-upon view, is that the judge should ask the confessor about the location because it affects the application of the hadd punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the textual variant
Locate the phrase 'wa la yus'alu al-muqirr 'an al-makan' in the text. Recognize that this is a statement from Fath al-Qadir.
This is the variant that is disputed.
2
Recognize the corruption
Note the comment from al-Nahr that this phrase is a tahrif (corruption) in some copies. Understand that a single consonant change (e.g., yus'alu vs. yus'al) alters the ruling.
The correct reading is 'yus'alu' (he is asked).
3
State the correct ruling
Affirm the mufta bihi position: the confessor must be asked about the place of the alleged theft. This is a procedural obligation on the qadi.
This ensures that the theft occurred in dar al-Islam where hadd applies.
4
Understand the legal rationale
The location matters because theft in dar al-harb does not incur the hadd punishment (cutting of the hand). The qadi must verify to avoid wrongful application.
This is based on the Hanafi principle that hudud are suspended in dar al-harb.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وفي فتح القدير ولا يسأل المقر عن (المكان ذكر في النهر أن ذلك وقع في بعض النسخ قال: وكأنه تحريف والصواب أنه يسأل
His saying: (And in Fath al-Qadir, and the confessor is not asked about the place) It was mentioned in al-Nahr that this occurred in some copies; he said: It is as if it is a corruption, and the correct is that he is asked.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This short passage addresses a textual discrepancy in the matn. The phrase from Fath al-Qadir states that the confessor is not asked about the place. However, the commentator in al-Nahr notes that this version is likely a corruption; the correct ruling is that the confessor should be asked about the place, just as witnesses are, due to the possibility that the theft occurred in dar al-harb where no cutting applies.

Key Terms
المقر (al-muqirr): The person who confesses; in this context, the thief who admits.
تحريف (tahrif): Textual corruption; an alteration of the original wording.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view (al-mufta bihi), what should the judge do regarding the location of theft?
A) Assume the theft occurred in dar al-Islam and proceed with hadd.
B) Ask the confessor where the theft took place.
C) Not ask, because the confession is enough.
D) Ask only if the thief is a non-Muslim.

Key Takeaway
The judge must ask the confessor about the place of theft to ensure it occurred in dar al-Islam, where the hadd punishment is applicable.

Presence of Witnesses at Hadd Cutting: Qiyas vs. Istihsan
Intra-madhhab dispute on witness presence at execution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi opinions on witnesses' presence at the hadd cut, explain the basis of each (qiyas and istihsan), and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Witness presence at execution is required by qiyas, but istihsan dispenses with it for practical ease.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores whether the two witnesses to a theft crime must be physically present when the hadd cut is carried out. The original matn asserts their presence is necessary, but later Hanafi authorities introduce an istihsan exception, creating an intra-madhhab dispute. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your grasp of how qiyas and istihsan interact in penal law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is the execution of the hadd cut for theft. The default ruling (from the matn) is that the two witnesses must be present; if absent or dead, the cut is not carried out.
This strict view is based on qiyas (analogy to the requirement of witnesses at the time of proving the crime).
2
Recognize the exception for rajm and qisas
The matn exempts rajm (stoning for zina) because the witnesses themselves must initiate the stoning. Qisas is carried out even without witnesses by istihsan, as it is a private right.
The exception for qisas is mentioned as istihsan, hinting at the flexibility of the Hanafi method.
3
Identify the later opinion (istihsan)
Al-Ramli reports that the later correct opinion from Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn is that witness presence is not required for the cut. This is based on istihsan (juristic preference) considering ease and the aim of punishment.
Thus there are two conflicting views within the school: the strict qiyas and the lenient istihsan.
4
Determine the mufta bihi (operative opinion)
The passage indicates that the later opinion (istihsan) is the one relied upon. Therefore, in giving fatwa, witnesses need not attend the execution.
This reflects the Hanafi principle of adopting the more practical and lenient view when the evidence allows.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (واعلم أنه لا بد من حضور الشاهدين وقت القطع كحضور المدعى حتى لو غابا أو ماتا لا قطع وهذا في كل الحدود إلا في الرجم ويمضي القصاص وإن لم يحضروا استحساناً؛ كذا في كافي الحاكم وإن شرط بداءة الشهود بالرجم. قال الرملي : وفي شرح منظومة ابن وهبان لابن الشحنة ولا يشترط حضور الشهود للقطع على الصحيح الأخير من قول الإمام، وكذا عندهما، وكذلك بعد موت الشهود ففي المسألة قولان قياس واستحسان والله تعالى أعلم.
His saying: (And know that the presence of the two witnesses at the time of cutting is necessary like the presence of the plaintiff. So if they are absent or die, there is no cutting. And this applies in all hudud except in rajm. And qisas is carried out even if they do not attend, by istihsan. As in Kafi al-Hakim, even if the witnesses' beginning with rajm is a condition. Al-Ramli said: In the commentary of Ibn Wahban's poem by Ibn al-Shihnah: The presence of the witnesses for cutting is not required according to the final correct opinion of the Imam, and likewise with the two companions, and also after the death of the witnesses. So in the matter there are two opinions: qiyas and istihsan. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage discusses the requirement of witnesses' physical presence at the execution of the hadd cut. According to the matn, they must be present, otherwise the cut is not carried out. This applies to all hudud except rajm (stoning) because rajm requires the witnesses to initiate the stoning. Qisas (retribution) is carried out even without witnesses as it is a private right. However, al-Ramli notes a later opinion from the Imams that witness presence is not a condition, based on istihsan. Thus there are two views: the strict view (qiyas) requiring presence, and the lenient view (istihsan) not requiring it.

Key Terms
الحد (al-hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Allah for specific crimes (e.g., theft, zina).
القطع (al-qat'): Amputation of the hand as a hadd punishment for theft.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference; deviating from an analogy due to a stronger consideration (ease, public interest, or a clear text).
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning; extending a ruling from an established case to a new case based on a shared effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the final correct opinion (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, must the two witnesses be present at the time of the hadd cut?
A) Yes, they must be present.
B) No, their presence is not required.
C) Only if they request to attend.
D) Only in cases of theft, not other crimes.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's mufta bihi position is that witness presence at the hadd cut is not required, overriding the strict qiyas view through istihsan.

Exception of Rajm from Witness Presence Requirement
Clarifying that rajm is excluded from the rule of witness presence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exception of rajm from the general rule requiring witness presence in hudud and explain the procedural reason for this exception.

Core Idea
Rajm requires witnesses to physically begin the stoning, so their presence is indispensable.

In Hanafi criminal law, the execution of hudud punishments generally requires the presence of the witnesses who testified. However, rajm (stoning for zina) is a unique exception. This lesson refines that rule, clarifying that while other hudud may proceed even if witnesses are absent or deceased, rajm drops entirely because the witnesses must personally initiate the stoning. This distinction is rooted in the Quranic command and practical necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Recall that for most hudud (e.g., cutting for theft, lashing for zina), the witnesses must be present at the execution. However, the passage states an exception.
The general rule is that absence or death of witnesses stays the hadd.
2
Locate the Exception
The passage explicitly excludes rajm from this rule. Find the phrase 'sawa rajm' (except rajm).
3
Understand the Reason
Rajm requires the witnesses to begin the stoning (bada'at al-shuhud). This is based on the Quranic verse 'And let a group of believers witness their punishment' (Surah An-Nur, 24:2), interpreted as requiring witnesses to participate in the execution.
Für lashing, witnesses are not required to participate; their presence is for testimony, not execution.
4
Recognize the Practical Consequence
If witnesses are absent or die after testimony, rajm is dropped entirely. However, lashing (jald) may still proceed, and qisas (retaliation) is carried out by istihsan because it is a personal right.
Note the istihsan reasoning for qisas: it is from the rights of people (huquq al-'ibad).
5
Note the Intra-Hanafi Nuance
The passage mentions that Abu Hanifa initially differed from his companions on the general rule, but later agreed that cutting (for theft) proceeds even if witnesses are absent. This refinement applies to all hudud except rajm.
The final mufta bihi position is that only rajm requires witness presence at execution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وهذا) في كل الحدود سوى الرجم قال في الشرنبلالية بعد أن ذكر أن ذلك وقع في النهر أيضاً وإن المؤلف وأخاه تبعا صاحب الفتح. قلت: استثناء الرجم مخالف لما تقدم لهم في حد الزنا بالرجم أنه إذا غاب الشهود أو ماتوا سقط الحد فلا يتجه إلا استثناء الجلد فيقام حال الغيبة والموت بخلاف الرجم لاشتراط بداءة الشهود به وهذه عبارة الحاكم في الكافي : وإذا كان أي المسروق منه حاضراً والشاهدان غائبان لم يقطع أيضاً حتى يحضروا. وقال أبو حنيفة بعد ذلك : يقطع وهو قول صاحبيه وكذلك الموت، وكذلك هذا في كل حد وحق سوى الرجم ويمضي القصاص وإن لم يحضروا استحساناً لأنه من حقوق الناس اهـ. فهذا تصريح الحاكم اهـ ملخصاً. قلت : وكان المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى استشعر بذلك فقال بعد ما نقله عن الكافي : وإن
His saying: (And this) applies to all hudud except rajm. He said in al-Sharnablaliyyah after mentioning that this occurred in al-Nahr as well, and that the author and his brother followed the author of al-Fath. I say: The exception of rajm contradicts what was previously stated for them in the hadd of zina by rajm, that if the witnesses are absent or die, the hadd drops. So no direction except the exception of lashing, which is carried out in case of absence and death, unlike rajm because the beginning of the witnesses is required. And this is the expression of al-Hakim in al-Kafi: And if the victim is present and the two witnesses are absent, he is not cut until they attend. And Abu Hanifa later said: He is cut, and this is the statement of his two companions, and likewise death. And this applies in every hadd and right except rajm, and qisas is carried out even if they do not attend by istihsan because it is from the rights of people. So this is the explicit statement of al-Hakim, summarized. I say: The author, may Allah have mercy on him, sensed that, so he said after what he quoted from al-Kafi: And if...

Commentary
This passage refines the previous ruling by specifying the exception of rajm. While other hudud require witness presence, rajm is special because the witnesses themselves must begin the stoning. If they are absent or dead, the rajm penalty drops entirely, unlike lashing (jald) which may still be carried out. The commentator clarifies the correct position from al-Kafi, noting that Abu Hanifa and his companions later opined that cutting can proceed even if witnesses are absent, except in rajm. Qisas (retribution) is carried out even without witnesses as it is a personal right. The text is cut off at the end.

Key Terms
بداءة الشهود (bada'at al-shuhud): The witnesses beginning the stoning in rajm; they must physically start.

Key Takeaway
Rajm uniquely requires witnesses to physically initiate the punishment; their absence or death drops the hadd.

Ruling on Multiple Thieves: Conditions for Hadd Cutting
Explains the ruling when multiple thieves steal together

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the conditions for hadd cutting when multiple thieves cooperate and identify the exception when there are multiple victims.

Core Idea
Each thief must individually take nisab to be cut.

When thieves work together, the hadd of cutting is not automatically applied to all. The Hanafi school carefully examines each thief's individual share, their relationship to the victim, and their mental capacity. This lesson unpacks the key conditions from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary, showing you how to determine when the cut is obligatory and when it is not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is group theft. The ruling: each thief is cut only if the value he personally took reaches nisab (10 dirhams or 1 dinar).
2
Check the condition of taking
There is no difference between direct taking and indirect causing (tasabbub). Both trigger the cut if nisab is reached.
3
Verify the absence of preventers
Certain persons prevent the cut: a mahram relative of the victim, a child, insane, or imbecile. If any such person is among the thieves, the cut is not applied.
This condition applies to each individual thief.
4
Confirm cooperation (ta'awun)
The thieves must have cooperated, either by starting together or one following immediately after the other. The commentary explains that cooperation is achieved even if they leave the safe place at different times but in close succession.
Cooperation is a condition for the group theft ruling; otherwise each is judged individually.
5
Apply the exception for multiple victims
If one thief steals from ten people, one dirham from each, he is not cut because his total from each victim is less than nisab. He is only liable for the value of the stolen property.
This reinforces that the nisab is per victim context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو جمعا والآخذ بعضهم قطعوا إن أصاب لكل نصاب) أي لو كان السارق جماعة لأن الموجب سرقة النصاب، ويجب على كل واحد منهم بجنايته فيعتبر كمال النصاب في حقه، وقدمنا أنه لا فرق بين كون الأخذ مباشرة أو تسبباً ولا بد من أن لا يكون فيهم ذو رحم محرم من المسروق منه ولا صبي ولا مجنون ولا معتوه وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا كانوا خرجوا معه من الحرز أو بعده من فوره أو خرج هو بعدهم في فورهم لأن بذلك يحصل التعاون. وقيد بالجمع لأنه لو سرق واحد من عشرة من كل واحد منهم درهماً من بيت واحد والظاهر أنه خاص في حق تضمينه المال فقط لما أنه لا يقطع بالنكول وأنه لو أقر ثم هرب لا يتبع.
He said: 'And if they are many and the takers among them, they are cut if each gets a nisab.' Meaning: If the thieves are a group, because the cause is stealing the nisab, and each one is obligated by his own crime, so the completeness of nisab is considered in his right. We have already stated that there is no difference between taking directly or indirectly. It is necessary that among them there is no one with a prohibited relationship to the victim, no child, no insane person, no imbecile. He (the author) gave it unrestricted, so it includes if they came out with him from the safe place or after him immediately, or if he came out after them immediately, because by that cooperation is achieved. He restricted it to many because if one person stole from ten people one dirham each from one house, the apparent is that it is specific only to the right of guaranteeing the money, because he is not cut for nusul (default), and if he confessed then fled, he is not followed.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a legal ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, commenting on the case of multiple thieves. The ruling states that when a group steals, the hand of each thief is cut only if the value of the stolen property taken by each individual reaches the nisab. This is because the obligation of cutting is based on each thief's own act of taking. The text clarifies that direct as well as indirect taking (tasarub) are considered. Additionally, certain persons cannot be among the thieves for the cut to apply: a relative within prohibited degrees (mahram) of the victim, a child, an insane person, or an imbecile. The commentary expands that the thieves must have cooperated in the theft, either by beginning together or one following immediately after the other. The restriction to a group is significant: if one thief steals from ten people, each one dirham, from one house, the cut is not applied because the nisab is not reached from a single victim. However, he is liable for the value of the property. Also, if a thief confessed and then fled, he is not pursued for the cut.

Key Terms
النصاب (al-nisab): The minimum value of stolen property that triggers the hadd cut; generally 10 dirhams or 1 dinar in Hanafi fiqh.
الحرز (al-hirz): A secure place where property is stored; stealing from a hirz is a condition for cutting.
التسبب (al-tasabbub): Causing the taking indirectly; considered equivalent to direct taking for liability and cutting in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for the hadd cutting to apply on a group of thieves?
A) The total stolen must reach nisab.
B) Each thief's individual share must reach nisab.
C) At least one thief must be an adult.
D) The thieves must be unrelated to each other.

Key Takeaway
For hadd cutting on multiple thieves, each thief must individually take a nisab, cooperate with others, and be free from preventers like being a mahram relative, child, insane, or imbecile.
